===== PAGE 1 =====
Ted and Eunice met at the Sunday School assignment
meeting at Rabbi Tofield’s home. Eunice almost didn’t attend.
The Temple synagogue had offered her an attractive teaching
position. Philip Selber, Chairman of the School Committee,
convinced Eunice that her place was at the Center and that
great changes were about to happen with the arrival of the
new Education Director he had just hired.
Eunice stayed on as a teacher at the Center, and in 1948,
accepted not only the Pilton Memorial Cup for having the
outstanding Sunday School class, but also a proposal of
marriage from Ted.
Raising children is never easy. For Ted, it was especially
challenging because he felt in many ways responsible for
each child growing up at the Center. Eunice, a teacher herself,
understood; but for his daughters, it
was sometimes difficult for them to
share their father with all the other
kids. But Ted and Eunice filled their
home with love and the richness of
Jewish living. Over the years, family,
friends and community leaders have
shared wonderful holiday meals with
the Gross Family.
Attention to Details...
By the end of the ‘50s, Mr.
Gross had our educational system in
high gear. Afternoon Hebrew School
met in two groups, Monday &
Wednesday and Tuesday & Thursday. A staff of 20 teachers
and administrators were employed for the 476+ students who
attended Sunday School. Education was so popular there were
even summer sessions.
In the 1959 season, 37 teens were Confirmed. Over 40
children participated in the Kindergarten Graduation, which
was followed by a luncheon for parents and friends. In 1962,
the Center began its Foundation School, the forerunner of
today’s Solomon Schechter Day School. By 1965, there were
evening classes for Hebrew High School, which included a
dinner hour. A Post Bar Mitzvah Torah reading program was
instituted.
The Confirmation Service of 1973 was dedicated to Ted
Gross for his then 24 years as Educational Director. On that
occasion, Philip Selber described Ted Gross in these words:
“He is ‘where the action is’... where the generation gap
not only shows but oft becomes painfully obvious ... It is
against this background that the true value of the dedicated
service of Ted Gross becomes clear, as we recall the unstinting
contributions of his talents and energies ... his unselfish
willingness to labor on a ‘one-to-one’ basis with the individual
student or to meet repeatedly in personal conferences with an
anxious parent ... his intense searching for the elusive key to
the motivation of a drifting student ... his pioneering efforts
in making the ‘art of Torah reading’ a status symbol among
the young ... his tenacious consistency in fighting for
standards in Jewish education against almost insurmountable
lethargy and opposition ... his continuance in the role of
classroom teacher of high school students despite increasing
administrative pressures ... his ever-present optimism in
working for a ‘break through’ with the child whose absenteeism
from school and Sabbath services makes any achievement a
small miracle... his love for intense Jewish living, and his own
personal commitment to Jewish observance, all portray and
exemplify the devotion and dedication with which he meets
the challenge of his role as an educator of the Jews of
tomorrow.
“Perhaps the best indicia of his contributions to the
community can be seen only from the view afforded by the
passing of time — the view of his many former students,
long graduated from school, still returning to our synagogue
and to synagogues elsewhere to read the Torah, of others
who have gone on to higher levels of Jewish education and
of those who have become prominent as laymen and as
professionals in the leadership of our congregation and
congregations elsewhere.”
Those words are as meaningful today as they were then.
With a deep love and devotion to Torah,
Theodore Gross lead our education
department from its early days, through the
building of a modern classroom wing up to
the development of a modern Day School.
Most of our current Center leaders are the
product of the excellent Jewish educational
programs implemented by Ted Gross. Many
more of us have fond memories of our
Hebrew School days and the role Ted
played in them.
Today, Ted is the sage of our Torah
program. For many years, he found readers
for each Torah portion, week in and week
out. He took special care to know and ask each post-Bar/Bat
Mitzvah to read a portion from their own sedra. Recently he
gave up full-time responsibility, but remains the Center’s
revered Baal Koreh.
“He who honors the Torah is honored by mankind.”
— Ethics of the Fathers
On behalf of the congregation, the Center’s Officers
and Board, Staff and Professionals wish Ted, Eunice and their
family a heartfelt mazel tov and yasher koach on this well
deserved honor.
Senator Bob Graham attended Eunice and
Ted’s Passover Sedar in 1990.
The Family Man...
Eunice Davis and Theodore Gross were married at the
Center on June 11,1949. They began a family right away with
the birth of their first
daughter Carol Marie in
1950. Daughter Beverly
Rieka was born in 1953.
Busy as they were
with careers and small
children, Ted and Eunice
made time to continue
their own educations.
They drove to Gainesville
one evening a week to
work on their degrees in
education — Ted’s
Eunice and Ted on their honeymoon. Master’s and Eunice’s
Bachelor’s. Raela Moss
went with them to take courses as well. These “nights out”
included a 30-mile round trip for Ted to get a baby sitter. With
only one class a week, they even drove to Gainesville during
a hurricane. It was worth it though. Ted received his Master of
Education from the University of Florida on June 8,1954.

Caterer
Margo’s Catering
Following a very successful year as preferred caterer at the Jacksonville Jewish
Center, Margo Ruby’s Catering has entered a lease arrangement with the Center to
be the exclusive caterer for all in-house, congregational and private functions.
The same high quality menus and beautiful presentations that have been enjoyed
this year at life-cycle receptions and parties, will now be available to Center organizations,
clubs and schools, as well as for congregational celebrations and holidays. In addition
Margo’s Catering will service the Day School lunch program, board dinners and other
occasions.
While Margo’s Catering will provide complete and personalized food planning
services, Lori Schoettler will coordinate and schedule all aspects of event planning.
Maintenance & Housekeeping Staff
The maintenance and housekeeping staff work diligently to keep our building
clean and presentable at all times. Richard Ford, our Facilities Supervisor, takes
pride in his staff, and devotes much of his time to taking care of all the physical needs
required by the many events which take place throughout the year. Volunteers, event
planners and Center staff appreciate the special attention they receive from the
maintenance department. Richard and his staff offer invaluable support to building
restoration crews and outside vendors.
Richard Ford
Facilities Supervisor

===== PAGE 5 =====
Committees
Adult Education
The Jewish people have historically been called the
“people of the book” We have a tradition of love and
dedication to education, and Jewish education in particular,
as a lifelong pursuit of the highest esteem. To answer the
diverse educational needs of our congregation, the Adult
Education Committee, chaired by Dr. Harris Rittenberg
and Dr. Joanne Davis and with the guidance of Rabbi
David Gaffney, coordinated an ambitious program with a
wide variety of courses and speakers throughout the year.
Hebrew literacy, Talmud, synagogue and holiday workshops,
Firing Line and other discussion groups formed the basis of a comprehensive, ongoing curriculum. In addition,
Rabbi Gaffney met one Wednesday each month for a lively discussion with the Sisterhood about various modern-
day topics. Etta Drashin and Wendy Brezin taught basic Hebrew literacy courses. The Setzer-Levit Memorial
Lecture, Shabbaton and community-based engagements brought prominent speakers of national and international
acclaim. We invite you to avail yourself in the coming year of the exciting programs that are now being planned to
enrich your spiritual life.
Rabbi Reuvan Kimelman was the featured speaker at the Shabbaton
Weekend, underwritten by the Marilyn and Louis Safer Shabbaton Fund. Rabbi
Kimelman, a Yale doctoral scholar, is a professor of Rabbinic Literature at Brandéis
University, Senior Scholar of CLAL (the National Jewish Center for Learning and
Leadership), and among other teaching assignments has taught at the Hebrew
University in Jerusalem and the Jewish Theological Seminary of America. A well
published author, Dr. Kimelman is a dynamic, engaging speaker on a variety of topics.
He presented thought provoking discussions on Jewish mysticism, choosing Jewish
leaders and the impact of social acceptance on the American Jewish community.
New this year, Rabbi Gaffney gave a series of six lectures on spirituality entitled
“Seeking the Face of God — Judaism as a Spiritual Journey.” The lectures, which
were held on selected Wednesday evenings, were very well received, with seventy or
more adults attending each session. Rabbi Gaffney eloquently presented a new and
refreshing encounter with a way of life and literature that facilitates spiritual fulfillment.
He made suggestions through story, legend, song and meditation for reclaiming sacred
moments for our own lives.
The Jewish Community Shabbaton, sponsored by the Federation in cooperation
with all the synagogues, was an occasion for fellowship, spirituality and the exchange of
ideas in the inspiring atmosphere of Shabbat. The National Learning Center for Learning
and Leadership (CLAL), a motivating force for communal thinking, made presentations
at gatherings which were held at different synagogues throughout the weekend. Rabbi Irwin Kula conducted
informative and lively sessions from our pulpit during Shabbat morning services and at a study session after lunch.
It was a unifying and enlightening experience for the diverse members of the Jacksonville Jewish community.
The 4th Annual Family University, directed by Pam Maman, offered Solomon Schechter Day School
students and their parents an opportunity tq study together for a one-day curriculum of varied topics.
Rabbi Reuvan Kimelman
The Adult Education Committee with
Shabbaton speaker, Rabbi Reuvan Kimelman.

Tjhe Gate Petroleum Company
of Jacksonville, is proud to own
and operate three of the most
prestigious private membership
clubs in Florida— the Ponte
Vedra Inn & Club, Epping
Forest Yacht Club, and The
Lodge & Club. From this premier portfolio
of clubs, an exciting membership has
evolved...The Gate Governors Club.
A membership in the Governors Club
makes it possible to enjoy privileges at
any combination of two or more clubs
within the Gate family. Club
combinations are conveniently
packaged and are attractively priced
creating a tremendous value.
Governors Club members enjoy such
diverse features as a world class marina,
Atlantic Ocean beaches, championship gc
tennis, fitness and a luxury spa. A variety
of outstanding restaurants and an exciting
social calendar makes this membership
a desirable choice.
Fore more information on membership
opportunities and benefits available with

Special Events
Annual Center Raffle for Education
“Money Mania” reached a feverish
pitch, as hundreds of people participated in
the festivities at the Jacksonville Jewish
Center’s Annual Raffle for Education.
Event Co-chairs Stuart Herman and
Allison Bailys along with their entire raffle
committee delivered a fabulous evening. The
highlights included a spectacular buffet by
Margo’s Catering, a wind-blown money tunnel, various
game show vignettes, entertainment by the UNF Jazz
Combo and of course the drawings for valuable prizes .
Honorary Chairs Kim and David
Robbins were presented a special gift from
the Center, by President Mark Shorstein,
for their long-time support and dedication
to the raffle.
Congratulations to the law firm of Shorstein &
Kelly P.A. which won the $10,000 Grand Prize. Early
bird drawing winners Deena and Jim Richman received
2 badges to the TPC courtesy of Coca Cola. Many others
won fabulous prizes contributed by these generous
business:
The big winner was by far the Samuel and Esther
Galinsky Educational Programs which will reap the
benefits of this major fund-raiser.
By all accounts, this year’s raffle was a huge success.
Everyone enjoyed the food and the format and, most
importantly, the financial goal of raising $50,000 for
education was reached thanks to the generosity of our
patrons and ticket holders. An exciting live auction netted
an additional $6,000 for the evening’s proceeds. Everyone
associated with this year’s raffle is to be congratulated
for a job well done.
Event Go-Chairs
Allison Bailys and Stuart Herman

JJC Golf Classic
A Hole-In-One for Education
The JJC Golf Classic, played last November at the Ponte Vedra Ocean
Course, was not only a great financial success, but a GREAT TIME was
had by all who participated. A sold-out field teed off in glorious weather,
on a beautiful course. Camaraderie was high and the competition was keen.
Congratulations to all.
The tournament included a captain’s choice format, fabulous food
and great prizes. The day concluded with an awards ceremony and silent
auction. Proceeds of the event will be used to fund scholarships to the
Solomon Schechter Day School.

===== PAGE 26 =====
Organizations
Center Men’s Club
The Jacksonville Jewish Center Men’s Club is dedicated to the enrichment
of Center life and the Jacksonville Jewish Community. It provides an opportunity
for the men of our synagogue to work together supporting, sponsoring and
participating in programs that bring meaning to our youth, companionship to our
elders, and involvement in our Jacksonville Jewish community.
Our Men’s Club is also an active member of the Federation of Jewish Men’s
Clubs, an international organization dedicated to the ideals, philosophy and
traditions of Conservative Judaism. Through the support of the Federation, we
distribute hundreds of Yellow Holocaust Memorial candles to the families of our congregation, every Yom Hashoah. This
year we will continue the successful “Hearing Men’s Voices” program developed by FJMC - a
series of workshops dedicated to creating a forum for discussion and sharing issues relating to
being a Jewish man in today’s world. These workshops cover family, religion, society and health
in thought provoking and fulfilling agendas led by leading experts and professionals.
We are committed to our Center Youth with programs like the Yad Shel Chai (Hand of
Life) Award that rewards our youth for reading Torah, the Youth Achievement Award for outstanding
Confirmation students and presentation of a book to every Bar and Bat Mitzvah. We also work
closely with Rabbi Dov Kentof to support the Center youth organizations by helping out with
conventions and Religious School programs.
Last year, Men’s Club established the Horty Gendzier Summer Scholarship Fund for
deserving children. This fund provides financial aid for children to attend Camp Ramah or other
Jewish enrichment programs. We are proud to honor the memory of Horty Gendzier who was so instrumental in the success
of these programs.
We support the Jacksonville Jewish Federation and Jewish Family and Community Services through tzedakah programs,
and the community at large, by volunteering on Christmas to allow our friends of other faiths to celebrate their holiday with their
families.
We are visible friends of our synagogue as well. Each year we decorate the Center’s Goldman Sukkah. We also sell
sukkah-building kits, and help assemble them for families of our congregation . You can find Men’s Club members at the Lag
B’Omer Picnic every year selling hot dogs and cokes. We maintain a loyal committee of ushers for services for Shabbat and
the High Holidays. Men’s Club members sponsor, lead and participate in
Men’s Club Shabbat and Armed Forces Shabbat and take an active role in
preparing B’nai Mitzvah students of all ages by providing tutors and
sponsoring receptions.
Our New American Adult B’nai Mitzvah program earned our Men’s
Club First Place and Honorable Mention Torch Awards from the Federation
of Jewish Men’s Clubs in years past. We are currently pursuing new Torch
Awards for community service and other programs.
The Men’s Club is a great way for friends to have fun. Every summer
we unite for the infamous deep-sea fishing trip and take our families with us
to a Lizard Kings hockey game and a Jacksonville Suns baseball game. In the
fall, we “kick off” our new year with a
membership party featuring games of chance
and raffles while we watch a Jacksonville
Jaguars away game on a big screen TV.
All this and more is waiting you if you
are at least 18, male and a member of the
Jacksonville Jewish Center. Join now, we
need your fellowship.
— Dave

Community Agencies
Jacksonville Jewish Federation
8505 San Jose Blvd. Jacksonville, FL 32217
448-5000 Fax.- 448-5715 • www.jaxjewish.org
The Jacksonville Jewish Federation
serves as a central resource for our Jewish
community. In summary, the Federation
is dedicated to providing for the welfare
of every Jewish person living in
Jacksonville. Through a partnership with
the United Jewish Communities, formerly
known as UJA, we are equally committed
to the survival of, and quality of life for,
every Jew living in Israel and throughout
the Diaspora.
The five major local recipient
agencies of funds raised by the Federation
are the Jewish Community Alliance,
Jewish Family & Community Services,
River Garden Hebrew Home, Jacksonville
Jewish Foundation and the Solomon
Center members, Michael DuBow, Mark
Shorstein, Kim Israel and Lenny Maiman were
honored at the Federation’s Annual Meeting.
Schechter Day School. We are proud of the
invaluable services provided by these five
outstanding Jewish agencies. It is a
privilege to assist them in trying to meet
their goals.
Jewish education is extremely
important, and the Federation is proud to
support the Solomon Schechter Day
School, Beit Midrash and Etz Chaim Hebrew
Academy. Through the Joan Levin Gift of
Israel program, Federation is helping to
make the dream of a trip to Israel a reality
for Jewish teens in our community.
The Federation is involved with
community relations, leadership
development and Missions to Israel. We
will continue to work in cooperation with
our local agencies, UJC and the
synagogues to address the vital issues and
challenges in the entire arena of Jewish
continuity.
Our Board wishes members of the
Jacksonville Jewish Center a Happy and
Healthy New Year.
— Scot N. Ackerman, M.D., President
Alan Margolies, Executive Director

Jacksonville Jewish Foundation
4131 Sunbeam Road, Suite 275
Jacksonville, Florida 32257
Phone: 394-0720 • Fax: 394-0956
The Jacksonville Jewish Foundation is dedicated to accumulating permanent
assets which can provide a source of income to help support the stability and
continuity of the Agencies and Synagogues in Jacksonville. The Foundation
professionally administers lifetime and testamentary giving plans designed to:
• Assist individuals to achieve their personal charitable goals in the most tax-
advantaged manner.
• Accumulate enduring endowed resources for use in supporting special,
emergency, and future needs, including those not provided for by the Jacksonville
Jewish Federation’s annual campaign.
The Foundation exists as a partnership of Jacksonville’s Synagogues and
Agencies to assure a better future for all generations. Through the Foundation,
donors are provided with many ways to perpetuate their charitable interests through
a wide array of funding opportunities.
The Jacksonville Jewish Foundation congratulates Ted Gross for his splendid
work and dedication for the past 50+ years.

Religious Schools
Confirmation
Celebrated 6 & 7 Sivan 5760 • June 8- 10, 2000
The Biblical festival of Shavuot commemorates the giving of the Torah and Ten Commandments to the
Jewish people. It is natural that this festival should be celebrated with an accompanying sense of commitment to
Jewish life that Confirmation represents. Confirmands demonstrate the knowledge gained through the completion
of our Hebrew High program by full participation in Shavuot services. In addition, this class read essays they had
prepared on aspects of Jewish American Life.
The Confirmation Class of 2000 (L to R) Row 1: Andrea Glauberg, Lauren Bloom, Erin Frisch, Jessica
Lipsky, Cantor Aron Heller. Row 2: Rabbi David Gaffney, Lauren Mack, Crista Cohen, Alison Zisser, Casie
Zimmerman, Erica Mack, Rabbi Dov Kentof. Row 3: Meredith Robson, Lisa Rand, Esther Yegelwel. Row 4:
Jonathan Graff-Radford, Sam Horovitz, Justin Axelrod, Sean Pozin, Aaron Finck.
The Confirmation Class went on a camping retreat with Rabbi Dov
Kentof
Rabbi David Gaffney hosted a Confirmation Class Hanukkah get-

Special Events
Annual Congregational Meeting & Installation of Officers
On Sunday August 20, the
Setzer Social Hall was
overflowing with congregants
who gathered for one of the
most uplifting Annual Meeting
and Installation programs in the
Center’s history.
Far and away, the most exciting event of
the day was the performance by the Jewish
singing group Visions from Orlando. This
tremendously talented and energetic trio of
beautiful teenage girls enthralled the audience,
young and old alike, with their lively renditions
of familiar Hebrew melodies.Everyone agreed
they were fabulous. Many our teens are fired
up to follow in their footsteps.
Beginning at noon, over
400 members and new comers
enjoyed a delightful, complimentary brunch prepared by Margo’s
Catering and made possible by the generosity of supporters
of the congregation. The entire event committee, Robin
Allerding, Shirley Bielski, Laurie DuBow, Barbara Safer,
Lori Schoettler, as well as Richard Ford and his staff, are to
be commended for providing a
lovely atmosphere and well
orchestrated program.
The business of the day
included inspiring speeches by
Mark Shorstein, outgoing
President, and Michael
Shorstein, incoming President.
Past President Laurie DuBow
conducted a warm, personal
induction of the Officers and
Board of Directors for 2000-
2002. Philip Selber was singled out from a list of past
presidents for filling the office
three times over the past fifty
years.
Past President Marsha
Pollock, event coordinator, was
mistress of ceremonies for a
wonderful program that included
an historic “burning of the
Center’s mortgage.” led by the
DuBow, Selevan and Setzer families. Appreciation was expressed for the devotion
and financial support of all the families that made retirement of our mortgage
possible.
Michael DuBow, Vice President of
Education, showed an amazing publicity video of the
Solomon Schechter Day School that was written and
executed by Nancy Ruben Friedman. Starring in the
film was Day School student Hallie Morris,
daughter of Carol & Joel Morris.
Our sincere thanks go to the
following generous sponsors Of this
outstanding event:
Drs. Dina & Howard Fetner & Family
Dr. Larry & Phyllis Goldberg & Family
Madeline & Stuart Hecht & Family
Risa & Stuart Herman & Family
Carol & Joel Morris & Family
Marsha & Ronnie Pollock
Wendy & FredPozin & Family
The Shorstein Family
Shorstein & Kelly, P.A.
Minnie Schreiber
Seeman Zimmerman

Reflections on life with our father Ted Gross
by Carol Gross and Ricki Gross Manne
Growing up... our father wasn't
ours. Mom used to say she "lost us"
all to the synagogue—that we spent
more time there than at home. It was
true. So many hours were spent there
waiting—praying, studying, learning
. . . and waiting. We were always
waiting for Dad to do whatever he
had to do with his students, or his
scheduling. And then, we'd take his
students home — and they'd sit in the
front seat of the car and we, in the back!
Dad gave so much respect to each and
every one of his students and their families. I
guess I felt then, that we came second — that
we were taken for granted.
Then I grew up . . . and found myself
treating the children and families
I worked for with the same
respect; arid I suppose my
personal relationships came
second, too, for a while.
Today, I believe, as I feel I
always did, that my father is one of
the "righteous men" of the world.
And I know how lucky l am to feel his
love and his blessings upon me and my family
— from the bottom of his bottomless heart.
I know I speak for all of us when I say we
have all been blessed to have this man in our
midst and active in our lives.
We love you Pa,
Ricki and Ed,
Tsurit, Ariel, Aviad and Yaniv
Carol and Jesse
5
===== PAGE 51 =====
Scouting
Junior Girl Scout Troop 5
Junior Troop 5 had a great year looking at Planet Earth
in a different way as we worked on the “Sign of the Satellite,”
which teaches about the past and shaping the world of the
future.
On a camping trip to Fort Wilderness in Disney World,
the girls planned and cooked meals, shopped for groceries,
set up tents and enjoyed the Sabbath in a camp setting.
The scouts conducted fascinating interviews with 40
and 60 year olds to learn about inventions that exist today
that did not exist when each was 10 years old.
With a sleepover visit to the Museum of Science and
History, the girls found out about the night sky, ancient
cultures such as the Greek, Norse and American Indian and
learned to read star maps. The Sky Search badge was earned.
We learned about caring for the Earth through two
badges, Ready for Tomorrow and Ecology. There were
discussions about what companies could do to help care for
the Earth. Some suggestions were: not using wasteful
packaging, not polluting water and being energy efficient.
Each girl also learned about careers that affect our
present and future. They had to shadow someone who works
in a government, science, or technological career. We learned
about city planners, systems analysts, and network
administrators.
For our last badge, Celebrating People, we held a party
for the Brownies featuring France and Mexico. With piñatas,
a replica of the Eiffel Tower, music and food, everyone had
a great time learning about other cultures!
At the annual Lake-Man-Jose neighborhood Spring
campout, the troop also earned the Outdoor Creativity badge.
Girl Scouting is also about being good citizens by giving
back to the community. Sixty lunches were packed for Kids
Cafe as part of the first annual Mitzvah Day coordinated by
Shirley Jernigan.
Sarah Hunter, Sarah Pierce, Stephanie Shacter, and
Kelby Siddons were selected for the Gateway Council’s 6th
grade event based on historic St. Augustine in the 1740’s.
They helped sew and embroider authentic outfits, camped and
served as tour guides of the historic district. This is
considered a “wider opportunity” that prepares girls for
broader adventures in Girl Scouting nationally and
internationally!
Thanks to: Janis Fleet for serving as Cookie Mom for
a very successful annual Cookie Sale; to Jill Tager for her
help when we needed it; as well as all the other parents for
their wonderful support of their daughters and Troop 5!
— Helen Shacter and Shirley Jernigan, leaders.
Cadette/Senior Girl Scout Troop 969
On my honor I will try...
• a night canoe trip down the Santa Fe River by moonlight,
avoiding snakes, alligators, and bees’ nests.
• to cook an international meal from start to finish and
learn Ava Axelrod’s chocolate secrets!
to serve God and my country...
• by earning the Menorah award, for Jewish Girl Scouts
• by participating in Gateway Council’s Goodwill Days
clothing drive and a food drive for JFCS.
• by making new educational materials for classes at the
Humane Society.
to help people at all times...
• like bringing cookies to the firemen at Station #5 and
scrubbing a fire truck, participating in Lake-Man Jose
Girl Scout’s Mitzvah Day, entertaining children at the
Leukemia Society of America’s Holiday party.
and to live by the Girl Scout Law...
•camping at Ft. Wilderness, leading services and games.
• inviting Troop 5 bridging Juniors to our meetings as we
learned about careers.
• earning interest patches in Creative Cooking, Pet Care,
Exploring the Net.
• earning Leadership pins for work as CITs, assistant¬
directing plays and tutoring reading.
Many thanks to: Robin Morris for her perseverance
in working with the girls on the Menorah Award. A big Girl
Scout salute (and hugs) to all the parents for supporting Girl
Scout field trips and activities; to the Center for a wonderful
place to meet; and to all those who supported the troop during
the cookie sale.
Jan Lipsky- Leader; Jill Tager- Assistant Leader 1999-2000
For information on Cadette/Senior Girl Scouting
at the Jewish Center for 2000-2001, contact Helen
Shacter at 292-0412 or Girl Scouts of Gateway Council
at 388-4653.
Tami Yergin and her dad, Leon, paddled the Sante Fe River with
Cadette/Senior Girl Scout Troop 969.

===== PAGE 53 =====
Administration
Executive Director’s Message
As we enter the New Year
5761, the Jacksonville Jewish
Center is on the verge of attaining
several historic milestones.
Consider the following:
• We have just retired our
mortgage and have pledged
as a congregation to remain
mortgage free.
• We are in the midst of the
Restoration 2000 campaign and project
which will bring the Jacksonville Jewish
Center ’s facilities up to a first class
standard.
• Rabbi David Gaffney who has led our
congregation for the past 29 years will be
retiring and we have embarked on the
awesome challenge of looking for the next
spiritual leader to guide this synagogue
into the new Century.
• We are preparing to celebrate the
Jacksonville Jewish Center’s 100th
birthday in the fall of 2001.
To many congregations, any one of these
milestones would be significant on its own merits.
The fact that we are experiencing these almost
simultaneously is a testament to the character of
our unique synagogue.
These are indeed exciting times. And, while
these milestones point to a historic crossroads in
the life of our congregation, it is the future that is
so bright.
New members are
becoming actively involved,
adding to the fabric and spirit of
our synagogue. Interest from
prospective members is peaking.
As a result, our membership
committee has been expanded to
meet the challenges of a growing
community.
The Center’s commitment
to education has never been
greater. Our schools are thriving
and the synagogue’s Education Committees are
busy planning an exciting future. The Samuel and
Esther Galinsky Educational Endowment
continues to provide state of the art
enhancements, such as a fully equipped Selevan
Computer Lab, which benefits all of our
educational programs.
Fortunately, the Center is blessed with
extraordinary lay leadership and dedicated
professionals. This combination ensures that we
will never rest on our laurels that we will continue
to build for the future. The theme of the new
administration, “Initiative for Excellence”
summarizes this commitment.
Therefore, in this coming year, as we
celebrate our past and give shape to our future,
may we continue with the spirit and determination
that has enabled us to reach so many milestones
and have so much promise for the years to come.
On behalf of Edith, Sam and Max, we wish
you a Happy and Healthy New Year.
— Bruce
Bruce Horovitz
Executive Director

Community Agencies
River (¡ügíp|)) Garden
HEBREW HOME/WOLFSON HEALTH & AGING CENTER
11401 Old St. Augustine Road • 260-9020 • www.rivergarden.org
“Eldercare At Its Best”
_“Honor thy father and mother that thy days may be long . . .” It was this
commandment which inspired the founding of River Garden Hebrew Home in
1946. It was this commandment which nourished the love and care that for more
than fifty years has made River Garden a nationally recognized model of
excellence in its field. It was this commandment that made it necessary to create
a Home that is welcoming to families and encourages its use as an extension of
family space. River Garden residents are a part of the community, not apart from it!
The River Garden Hebrew Home has also become the anchor of a growing
system of elder services including the Home, The Coves, Family Care Support
program and Home Health Agency. The success of River Garden is based on the
tradition of meeting 100 percent of local Jewish community needs and of serving
rich and poor alike with excellence. The River Garden Foundation accepts
donations to help River Garden continue to meet its mission. This would not be
possible without substantial charitable support from the community and the work
of The River Garden Foundation to stimulate planned gift annuities, trusts and
bequests.
River Garden’s programs of short-term rehabilitative/respite care, long¬
term residential care, Alzheimers’ and Adult Day Care, serve over 180 people
on any given day. These programs are guided by a devoted, professional full
time staff of over 200. Staff includes physicians and beauticians; nurses, social
workers, pharmacists, activities specialists; physical occupational and speech
therapists; dieticians, etc. In addition, scores of dedicated volunteers help create
a special caring community.
Located on a 35 acre Mandarin campus containing lush Florida oak and
pine trees, a private lake, meandering walking paths, River Garden is the perfect
setting for residents and visitors. River Garden is a community where people
live, love and care; a community of many lifestyles and of rich Jewish content,
and a community which every day strives to live up to the mandate of the Fifth
Commandment.
In recent years, life on campus has become more active and attractive with
the completion of The Coves, the elegant, affordable retirement community.
River Garden

Now in its sixth year, this elegant
yet affordable retirement community is
located on River Garden’s 35 acre
campus in Mandarin.
Sponsored by the not-for-profit
River Garden Holding Company, The
Coves offers comfort, security, club¬
house living and the opportunity for
continued growth during the retirement
years in a Jewishly sponsored
envronment.
The River Garden Foundation is a philanthropic organization, established
to provide resources for programs and facilities to enhance the quality of life for
the aged. Its primary purpose is to fund the not-for-profit River Garden system of
services.
The foundation is dedicated to helping the elderly remain in control of their
own lives by assuring services to people at all levels of need and financial ability.
The aim of the Foundation is to keep pace with the changing needs of the
aging through programs that meet a broad array of health care needs, as well as
provide a full spectrum of residential options.

Community Agencies
Jewish Family & Community Services
3601 Cardinal Point Drive
Jacksonville, FL 32257-5582 • Phone 448-1933
Iris T. Young, Executive Director
Adopt-A-Senior
You can help support Kosher Nutrition, and the elderly in our community who rely
on the program, by “adopting” a senior. Call 448-1933 to learn more.
Mount Carmel
Gardens, Inc.
5846 Mt. Carmel Terrace
Jacksonville, FI. 32216
(904) 733-6696
Linda Rubens, R.N., N.H.A.
Executive Director
Adoption
JFCS continues to place babies into loving homes across the country, including
Florida, Connecticut and New York B- three states that require a license to place
children. Last year, we found adoptive families for approximately 90 babies.
Bus Rental
Now the community can rent the JFCS buses to shuttle guests to and from life cycle
events and family gatherings. Enjoy bar and bat mitzvahs, weddings and other special
occasions without the headache of coordinating rides for out-of-town guests.
Catering Service
With so much experience preparing good food, JFCS now caters brunches,
engagement parties, bar and bat mitzvahs and other life cycle events. The kitchen
provides delicious menus, tastefully presented, while observing dietary laws.
Community Kosher Nutrition Program
CKNP continues to provide hot, nutritious, kosher meals to the elderly at Mt. Carmel, in
a safe and friendly environment.
Counseling
JFCS provides quality mental health care by licensed professionals, at reasonable
rates. Confidentiality is always guaranteed. Services include counseling for grief,
depression, family issues, parent-child conflict, life transitions and much more.
Feed A Needy Neighbor
With donations of non-perishable food items from concerned community, JFCS
provides emergency groceries to families and individuals experiencing difficult times.
Jewish Healing Network
The Jewish Healing Network reaches out to those who are struggling, ill or dying
by sharing the rich resources within the Jewish tradition.
Senior Transportation
JFCS transports seniors to religious services, doctors appointments, shopping
centers and recreational activities for an affordable fee.
There’s So Much More...
These are just a few of the many services offered at JFCS. For those needs the
agency cannot address, staff is always available to refer you to the appropriate
resource.

Home Is Where The Heart Is
Mount Carmel Gardens apartments
was designed, even to the smallest detail,
to provide comfortable and pleasant
surroundings. From the initial concept,
Mt. Carmel Gardens has strived to create
respectable living for the elderly
community, providing more than
housing. Mt. Carmel Gardens offers a
17-story building on a beautifully
landscaped site, 24-hour staffing,
community facilities, and planned
programs, all of which were developed
as part of an over-all concept.. .a concept
of responding to the desires of retirees
for security, comfort, safety,
independence and the enrichment of
stimulating social-recreational activities
shared with others.
Mount Carmel Gardens is conve¬
niently located, with transportation,
shopping, hospital and doctor’s offices
nearby.

Sunday Sports - Basketball Program

athletic programs on Sunday afternoons. All the games and practices are held in the
Fletcher-Selber Auditorium of the Jacksonville Jewish Center. Thank you to Gayle
Bailys who coordinated a very successful program and to the volunteer coaches for
their valuable assistance and time. We look forward to an exciting 200-2001season.

Daisy Girl Scout Troop 176 had a fun-filled year! We renewed friendships that we hope will last forever We had
a great time with the many projects, activities and sing-a-longs. The girls especially enjoyed learning to sew, paint and
plant. The goals set by the Girl Scouts of America program were easily achieved by these caring, sharing and
ambitious young girls. We had a great group of girls that will make wonderful Brownies.
For more information, call Stacey Kohl, 230-2800.
Brownie Troops 258 and 882
Brownie Troop 882 had another wonderful and busy year.
During this year, the girls worked on many different “tryits”: animal,
creative composing, dancerize, good food, puppet, doll and plays,
and safety. They learned about each; then they either wrote or
discussed the different topics, explaining how, as Girl Scouts, it
related to them and their families.
At our annual Hanukkah party at Mt. Carmel we entertained
and gave gift baskets to the residents. Baking hamantaschen for
Purim was a delicious lesson.
We sold lots of boxes of cookies for the annual Girl Scout
Cookie Sale. Our troop also donated boxes of cookies to the Mandarin Food Bank, and received a patch for Community
Service.
The Brownies had great fun at the Girl Scout camp, Camp Chowenwaw. The girls enjoyed a roaring campfire,
and plenty of “sommores”. We walked along the shoreline of Black Creek, sang songs and had a great weekend!
It has been a great year and we are all looking forward to our next year of great activities.
We welcome new members to our troop and encourage parents to participate as well. For information contact
Dodi Kress, 737-3502, Laura Cagan, 260-9890, or Lynn Kluger, 221-5748,

Rabbi Kentof’s Message
As we enter the school year 2000/
2001, our Education & Youth
Department is taking a new look at an
old problem: How can we be sure our
young people will retain their Judaism
and excel in Judaica?
I agree with the group of
educators who believe the way to do
this is by offering young people diverse
and challenging opportunities to
experience their Judaism, both in
formal as well as informal situations.
Through a variety of hands-on
activities, designed to capture their imaginations and
encourage leadership and independence, we can help our
youth create memory banks which they can use to help
make the tough decisions they will face later on in their
lives - the right Jewish decisions.
Experiencing Judaism in a variety of ways - some
in the formal classroom setting, some informal - like
clubs and synagogue holiday celebrations, combined with
summer USY, Ramah, and Day Camp activities - helps
to create well-rounded individuals, who return to Judaism
because they choose to and because they are in love with
its traditions.
With this in mind we design, and
redesign, our Hebrew School and
Youth Programs. Every year we
endeavor to add new curriculum
materials, programs, and staff members
to keep our Hebrew School fresh and
exciting. And every year we bring in
new advisors and/or create new
programs and social action projects to
keep our youth clubs moving forward
and brimming with excitement. Of
course, we include plenty of camp outs
and conventions!
I hope and pray that you will take advantage of the
many opportunities offered at the Center to enrich your
family and keep them in the fold of Judaism, so that we
may grow “from generation to generation.”
I, my wife Alina and our children, Gil and Tali, join
together to wish you and yours a Happy, Sweet, and
Prosperous New Year.
- Rabbi Dov Kentof
Rabbi Dov Kentof
Director of Education & Youth

It is with great enthusiasm and expectation that I begin
my first year as president of the Jacksonville Jewish Center
Sisterhood. Through programs and projects geared toward
education, social action and religious observance, we will have
the opportunity to expand our knowledge and commitment to
Judaism.
Last year, our educational and religious programs featured
enlightening Sisterhood seminars led by Rabbi Gaffney, our
annual Sisterhood Shabbat and Women’s Minyan, with
participation by our able and talented members, as well as
informative book reviews. We also supported the youth of our
congregation with snacks during the High Holidays, apples and candy for Simchat Torah,
hamantaschen for Purim, and pen pals for college students.
Our financial support for the religious schools was provided through our Youth
Fund/Religious School donation, and with Leagrams for Consecration and Confirmation.
Donations from our fund raising activities provided scholarships to those children attending
Camp Ramah and the US Y on Wheels program. All of these successful projects will continue
throughout the coming year.
Our monthly program meetings were highlighted by a Torah study evening led by
Rebbitzin Karen Goldscheider, a stress management seminar, a new perspective on Hanukah
by Alina Kentof, and a wonderful array of Passover dishes and memories from Margo
Ruby and Shirley Bielski. The Torah Fund luncheon honored our own Barbara Safer, a Vice
President of the International Women’s League board, and an international trainer. Our
Torah Fund campaign last year raised a record amount of funds that were donated to the
Jewish Theological Seminary.
At the annual Women’s League Florida Branch conference in Fort Lauderdale,
Sisterhood was honored with a certificate on the 75th anniversary of our affiliation with
Women’s League. We have two Sisterhood members on the Florida Branch Board, and two
members on the International Board.
Maxine Romo
President
We had a very successful fundraising year with our Rosh Hashanah flower and card
sales, Nachas Taxes and Donor funds. These activities will continue to be a major part of our fundraising efforts. The
Sisterhood Judaica shop ha&.'proven to be an ongoing profitable enterprise, as well as benefiting all members of the congregation
by providing beautiful gift items, educational materials and ritual objects. The highlight of our fundraising activities last year
was the Champagne Brunch and Tour of Homes.
In order to maintain a vibrant and active Sisterhood, we ask all of you to join us in working towards our goal of growth
and commitment to Jewish ideals. Becoming involved is a
wonderful way to renew old friendships and make new ones.
Sisterhood can enrich your life.
Left to right: Phyllis Goldberg, Marsha Pollock, Maxine Romo, Beth
Shorstein and Bonnie Sandler attended the Florida Branch Spring
Convention, May 2000, in Ft. Lauderdale.
The Woman of Valor poem from Proverbs, 31, states,
“Let her works praise her in the gates.” Become, and continue
to be, an active member of Sisterhood. It will be a rewarding
experience for all of us.
Don and I wish you all a Shana Tovah, and a year filled
with peace.
— Maxine

Recreation
Center Day Camp — Making Memories for a Lifetime!
by Alex Whitman, Jr. Counselor
This year’s JJC Summer Camp was a blast!
It seems like the specialty camps have been everywhere and done everything from
riding waves at Surf Camp, to nailing the game winner at Basketball Camp, to taking a trip to
Cape JJC for Rocket Launch. Each week of camp featured a different specialty. They included
basketball, baseball, science, computers and more. “Judaica-on-Wheels” sent cards and
visited local hospitals, performed at Augustine Landing and planted a garden at River
Garden. For Cheerleading Camp, the Roar of the Jacksonville Jaguars cheerleaders teamed
up with our own future stars!
Our 2, 3 and 4 year olds had a great summer with
a wide variety of activities. They went blueberry
picking, took trips to the movie theater, and even visited
a pet store. They had lots of fun in art making snowmen
and beaches, among other projects. In Judaica, these
young campers were delighted with Bible stories about
Joseph and his brothers and David and Goliath.
Splashing at the pool for free swim was everyone’s
favorite.
Camp Yom Tov had a great time as well, going on
field trips to Adventure Landing, Laser Tag and the
Marine Science Center. These campers seem to always
be involved in games - like “Bombardment”, shooting
hoops, launching rockets or trying their luck at cards
with Mike Schultz.
That’s not all! Campers had a fantastic time
horseback riding, at a petting zoo, participating in a
Bike Rodeo, and watching a helicopter land on the
Center’s ball field. The Annual Camp Carnival was a
highlight, and the Talent Show and Raffle was a big success with lots of wonderful prizes.
For fun you won’t want to miss, come to the Center Day Camp next year and have the
summer of a lifetime!
Our thanks to the Day Camp Staff, Counselors, Jr. Counselors and C.I. T’sfor
an outstanding summer program:
Laura Cagan - Camp Yom Tov Director
Dodi Kress - Camp K’ton Director
Robin DeCrispino - CIT Director

Sharon Seebol, Vicky Finkelstein, Heather Ferman - Arts & Crafts Specialists
Edith Horovitz, Pam Maman, Rebecca Feyerick - Judaica Specialists
Mercedes Phillips - Day Camp Office Manager

How Young The World Is
A five-year-old boy, riding with his mother,
saw the steel work of a half-finished building
and asked her:
“Mother, is the building going up ...or down?”
To a child the clutter of construction
looks like the debris of destruction.
Clearly, to the precise eyes of childhood
half a building is only half a building.
How, then, can he know
in which direction the building is going?
Looking at the world around us
we are often as confused as the child.
We see a world in which some people want
to tear down what others are building up.
Why is this?
As the world is measured
we are no older than this child.
By the time-scale of the stars
the history of Man is only a few seconds.
In the light of eternity
how young the world is ...
And how unfinished.
Like the child, we need to ask
the direction in which the world is going:
the direction of Man himself.
We were given such a direction
at the beginning of civilization
a guide for us and the world to go forward.
We find this in the Ten Commandments
in the ten “Sayings” given at Sinai
when mankind was very young indeed
“even to us, to all of us, who are alive this day. ” *
They are our guides to maturity.
What, then, is the meaning of
the mistakes we continue to make?
Why is the world Man is building
still so far from the world Man wants?
Is it not because Man is still so young?
We know that a child will run away
from those who love him to get a toy
offered by someone else.
So, often, do we.
Yet we also know that a child
has the capacity to grow, to respond to life
to become increasingly awafe of reality.
So do we.
We know that a child
who does grow into a true adult
is one who has been given loving-guidance:
a direction in life given him by someone out of love.
This is what man has been given
in the Ten Commandments.
Let us measure the meaning of this gift
by looking at just one of the Ten Commandments:
“Thou Shalt Not Covet...”
To understand this Commandment
We must remember that
to covet is the opposite of to share.
When we covet what belongs to someone else
we feel insufficient inside ourselves.
To covet is a poverty of the spirit.
We cannot covet and grow at the same time.
How can we teach ourselves not to covet?
We must discover that each of us
already has far more potential within himself
of growth, of fulfillment, even of greatness
than he has yet developed.
For each of us is “a young world”
reaching to eternity
a world in himself wherein he can find
ever more without any need to covet.
We must also teach ourselves
to share with others our goals and possessions.
For when we share we cannot covet.
And as we give, we become more.
This was given to us at Sinai:
“. . . to all of us who are alive this day. ”
In the light of the Commandments given us
we often behave like children.
*Deutoronomy 5:3

— The Samuel & Esther Galinsky Educational Programs —
Solomon Schechter Day School
We all look for inspiration from time to time. It might be
from a family member, a rabbi, hazzan or respected teacher; it
might be from a book or a piece of text. We can also find
inspiration by walking through the halls of our school. Who
cannot be proud when the first siddur is presented to an eager
student? Who doesn’t marvel at our Science exhibits, Jewish
History Fair, Seders and art projects? Who can’t be inspired by
a thriving Jewish community of students, motivated teachers
and committed parents?
We are proud that we are doing our part, not only to ensure
quantity, but quality as well. While there is room for
improvement, I hope you agree that we do some remarkable
things at Schechter.
Such accomplishments do not take place in a vacuum. They are due to the combined efforts of
our dedicated faculty, as well as the commitment and work of our volunteers and supporters. The on¬
going work of our PTA, our committee members and our board cannot be minimized. The passion of
these individuals for the sake of our students provides us with tremendous inspiration.
As we look to the future, it is up to each and every one of us to maintain the excellence and the
standards that we have set at Schechter. Then, too, each one of us can be an inspiration to others.
— Willard Kennedy
Willard M. Kennedy

Religious Schools
Afternoon Hebrew School
The Afternoon Hebrew School of the Jacksonville Jewish Center is designed for students in grades 3-7, and provides an
elementary education leading to Bar/Bat Mitzvah and continuation in the high school program.
Meeting on Mondays, Wednesdays and Saturdays, “the basics” are at the core of the curriculum, with stress on Hebrew
reading, Jewish social studies, and current events relating to Israel. Synagogue skills, holiday observances and knowledge of
prayers are all part of the comprehensive Afternoon Hebrew School program.
Aleph Class: Teachers - Carole Goldberg, Alina Kentof Bet Class: Teachers - Carole Goldberg, Wendy Brezin
Students: Daniel Abramson, Lillian Anderson, Alyssa DeCrispino, Students: Michael Kessler, Corey King, Jordan Kress, Melissa
Craig Herring, Stephanie Seebol, Danielle Slavin and Emily Talpalar. Neadle, Danielle Palombo, Mark Safer, Paul Sandler, Molly Seebol,

Special School Events
Consecration 5760
February 12,2000
The Aleph classes of Solomon Schechter Day School
and Afternoon Hebrew School celebrated the official
beginning of their religious education with a beautiful
Consecration ceremony during Shabbat services. The students
demonstrated their knowledge and love of Judaism in a lovely
program highlighting the accomplishments of great Jewish
personalities of the 20th Century.
Solomon Schechter Day School Grade 1-A
Mrs. Bonnie Loesser, teacher; Mrs. liana Manasse and Mrs. Robin
Morris, Hebrew teachers. Class in alphabetical order: Erica Cagan,
Briana Finkelstein, Jennifer Gartner, Joshua Goranson, Michael Hall,
Garret Jaffe, Haley Rose Lanigan, Gad Noach Lee, Isaac Asher Pearl,
Rebekah Pollan, Larry Richter, Leah Robbins, Laura Sandler, David
Sherman and Alexandra Silverberg.
SSDS Seventh Grade Graduation
June 6,2000
On Demri, Dana Kresel, Zach Monis, Mathew Shorstein
and Shira Spalter (show left to right) celebrated their
graduation from the Solomon Schechter Day School with a
program honoring the Torah. Each student recounted the
highlights of one of the Five Books of Moses. The graduates
also reflected on their experiences in the Mitzvah Program,
citing Biblical sources for the mitzvot they performed as part
of their school cuniculum.
SSDS Middle School Trip to New York
May 8-11,2000
Sixth and Seventh graders put a new spin on their
American/Jewish experience with a busy three days of tours
that included Ellis Island, the Jewish Heritage Museum and
Central Park. At the Lower Eastside Tenement Museum,
students simulated the immigrant experience. They ate at
kosher restaurants, davened daily, walked through Borough
Park, cheered for the Yankees and absorbed the culture of the
Big Apple.
Consecration 5760
4- Afternoon Hebrew Aleph Class
Mrs. Alina Kentof and Mrs. Carole Goldberg, teachers teachers. Class
in alphabetical order: Daniel Abramson, Lillian Anderson, Alyssa
DeCrispino, Craig Herring, Stephanie Seebol, Danielle Slavin and Emily
Talpalar.
Solomon Schecter Day School Grade 1-B
Mrs. Paula Horn, teacher; Eileen Fischoff, teaching assistant; Mrs.
liana Manasse and Mrs. Robin Morris, Hebrew teachers. Class in
alphabetical order: Samuel Bacaner, Samuel Bernard, Alexandra Block,
Katie Dicker, Max Fleisher, Alec Goldman, Benjamin Hecht, Daya Kedem,
Gina Kluger, Emily Levine, Jean Ann Lipsky, Gabrielle Magid, Sara Plotkin,
Shira Rittenberg, Danielle Rogozinski, Max Rogozinski and Jenna Shuman.

===== PAGE 124 =====
Community Agencies
Jacksonville Jewish Federation
8505 San Jose Blvd. Jacksonville, FL 32217
448-5000 Fax.- 448-5715 • www.jaxjewish.org
The Jacksonville Jewish Federation
serves as a central resource for our Jewish
community. In summary, the Federation
is dedicated to providing for the welfare
of every Jewish person living in
Jacksonville. Through a partnership with
the United Jewish Communities, formerly
known as UJA, we are equally committed
to the survival of, and quality of life for,
every Jew living in Israel and throughout
the Diaspora.
The five major local recipient
agencies of funds raised by the Federation
are the Jewish Community Alliance,
Jewish Family & Community Services,
River Garden Hebrew Home, Jacksonville
Jewish Foundation and the Solomon
Center members, Michael DuBow, Mark
Shorstein, Kim Israel and Lenny Maiman were
honored at the Federation’s Annual Meeting.
Schechter Day School. We are proud of the
invaluable services provided by these five
outstanding Jewish agencies. It is a
privilege to assist them in trying to meet
their goals.
Jewish education is extremely
important, and the Federation is proud to
support the Solomon Schechter Day
School, Beit Midrash and Etz Chaim Hebrew
Academy. Through the Joan Levin Gift of
Israel program, Federation is helping to
make the dream of a trip to Israel a reality
for Jewish teens in our community.
The Federation is involved with
community relations, leadership
development and Missions to Israel. We
will continue to work in cooperation with
our local agencies, UJC and the
synagogues to address the vital issues and
challenges in the entire arena of Jewish
continuity.
Our Board wishes members of the
Jacksonville Jewish Center a Happy and
Healthy New Year.
— Scot N. Ackerman, M.D., President
Alan Margolies, Executive Director

Jacksonville Jewish Foundation
4131 Sunbeam Road, Suite 275
Jacksonville, Florida 32257
Phone: 394-0720 • Fax: 394-0956
The Jacksonville Jewish Foundation is dedicated to accumulating permanent
assets which can provide a source of income to help support the stability and
continuity of the Agencies and Synagogues in Jacksonville. The Foundation
professionally administers lifetime and testamentary giving plans designed to:
• Assist individuals to achieve their personal charitable goals in the most tax-
advantaged manner.
• Accumulate enduring endowed resources for use in supporting special,
emergency, and future needs, including those not provided for by the Jacksonville
Jewish Federation’s annual campaign.
The Foundation exists as a partnership of Jacksonville’s Synagogues and
Agencies to assure a better future for all generations. Through the Foundation,
donors are provided with many ways to perpetuate their charitable interests through
a wide array of funding opportunities.
The Jacksonville Jewish Foundation congratulates Ted Gross for his splendid
work and dedication for the past 50+ years.

Building Fund Campaign
yfrottfrOrwiil* y
RESTORATION 2000
a commitment to excellence in the new Century
The goal of the Restoration 2000 project is to bring the facilities of the Jacksonville Jewish Center up
to a first class standard. The Center facility has had tremendous use over the past 25 years, and the wear and
tear is evident. Previous Building Fund campaigns have specially targeted retiring the mortgage. The recent
Centennial Challenge Campaign addressed many of the major repairs and refurbishments that had been
postponed over the years.
With the mortgage retired and the congregation approaching its Centennial in the year 2001, the
opportunity presents itself to restore the most highly visible areas of our facility to reflect the Center’s
commitment to excellence in the next Century.
The Jacksonville Jewish Center provides a forum for a myriad of activities, educational and entertainment
opportunities, congregational and individual lifecycle events, as well as religious serviqes.
For example, in the 1999-2000 season alone, 26 babies had brits or babynamings, 40 children were
Consecrated, 37 students celebrated Bar or Bat Mitzvahs, 17 teens were Confirmed, 10 couples were married
on our pulpit. Furthermore, receptions were held in the Benjamin Setzer Social Hall or the Fletcher-Selber
Auditorium for the hundreds of people who attended these special occasions.
In that same period, over 400 children were educated through the Samuel and Esther Galinsky
Educational Endowment Program which encompasses the Early Childhood and Extended Day Programs, the
Solomon Schechter Day School and Afternoon Hebrew School. Book Fairs, Jewish History Fairs, plays,
programs, talent shows, award ceremonies, assemblies, youth conventions and many more extra curricular
activities were conducted in the various halls and meeting rooms of the Center.
Add to the list the thousands who worship herein the High Holidays, Shabbats and festivals, and
upwards to a thousand who attend Performing Artists concerts.
People have passed through the lobby of the Jacksonville Jewish Center 365 days a year for over 25
years, on their way to some wonderful personal experience. The Restoration 2000 project will create an
atmosphere that will enhance the enjoyment and fond memories of future events for our congregants and
guests.
After careful consideration of several highly recommended design firms, the Restoration 2000 Design
Committee selected Levin/Brown & Associates, Inc., to direct the million+ dollar project. Levin/Brown, a Baltimore-
based firm, has a national reputation for unique synagogue designs and renovations that nourish the ideals of
our Jewish heritage. The principals of the firm are actively involved in synagogue life through their professional
experience and their personal commitment to the development of the Jewish institution. Jay Brown, AIA, is
working directly with our congregation to make enhancements to our building that will provide an upscale
backdrop for the many congregational and private occasions celebrated each year at the Center.
The Restoration 2000 Design Committee is pleased to recognize the following contributors, as of
August 1, 2000:

In Honor of Theodore Gross
a living treasure of the Jacksonville Jewish Center
For over 50 years Theodore
Gross has devoted his life to the
religious education of our youth as
Educational Director, teacher and
mentor. Mr. Gross ushered in a
modern era of institutional Jewish
education. In addition, Ted has
personally nurtured a love of Torah
and the faithful reading of our most
sacred texts in hundreds of Bar and
Bat Mitzvahs. Through his efforts,
the Center has a skilled cadre of baal
korim who read Torah on Shabbat
and holidays.
In the Beginning...
Ted was bom to Louis and Liba Gross in Brooklyn, New
York, on June 27,1917. His warm, close-knit family instilled a
love of Judaism and learning in Ted from an early age. He
began elementary school at PS 186, and after three years was
transferred to the Yeshiva Rabbi Chaim Berlin, where he studied
until eighth grade. A devoted student, Ted made a 90 minute
trip morning and evening to attend Isaac Elchanan Yeshiva
High School. The ambitious program at the Yeshiva included
Hebrew studies from 9 a.m. to 3 p.m., and general studies from
3 to 6 p.m., with public school teachers from Washington
High School Upon graduation, Ted entered Yeshiva College
and later, its Teacher’s Training Institute, from which he
received a Bachelor of Arts in 1940.
As a Young Man...
Ted secured a fine teaching position at the Harrisburg
Community Center School in Pennsylvania, but after only two
years was drafted by the U.S. Army to service in World War II.
His education, however, allowed him to test for the Army
Specialized Training Program. Ted, who had wanted to teach
physics, was delighted to be accepted into the ASTP electrical
engineering course at Carnegie Institute of Technology in
Pittsburgh, PA. Ted sailed through his 3 Vi years of study and
was able to find living accommodations that allowed him to
retain his religious lifestyle. In fact, it was his devotion to
Judaism that kept Ted from becoming a professional electrical
engineer upon completion of his military duty. After graduation
from Carnegie Tech, the Army sent him to the Philippines and
the Japan. There, his commanding officer pointed out to Ted
that electrical engineers worked regularly on Saturday. So,
Ted returned to teaching.
The Educational Professional...
After his honorable discharge from the Army, Ted took
a position in a Hebrew Day School in Johnstown,
Pennsylvania. Hearing of an opening for an Education Director
at a synagogue in Jacksonville, Florida, Ted sent his resume
to the Jewish Theological Seminary.
That summer, Philip Selber, Harry Gendzier and other
delegates from the Jacksonville Jewish Center were scheduled
to attend the 1947 United Synagogue of America Convention
in New York City. The Seminary arranged for them to interview
Theodore Gross for that important staff position. The meeting
went well and Ted was hired on the spot.
In September 1947, Mr. Gross came to Jacksonville
to be the Education Director at the Center, then located in
Springfield. Among his responsibilities were the
administration of the Hebrew School, Sunday School,
Nursery-Kindergarten, Summer Day Camp, and taking
charge of the Youth Activities. He applied progressive,
organizational methods to religions
education programs, and
developed a transportation system
that allowed Jewish children from
all over the city to attend afternoon
Hebrew school and Shabbat
morning services.
In April of 1948, Dr. Azriel
Eisenberg, Director of the
Philadelphia Council on Jewish
Education visited and inspected
our schools. In his report, Dr.
Eisenberg observed, “On the
whole, I was greatly encouraged by
what I saw. You have a fine group
of children who are imbued with a
positive attitude and good self-discipline. You have a good
principal [Ted], who is devoted and capable. . . . You have
unusual opportunities to make the Jacksonville Jewish Center
one of the outstanding schools in the country. You are already
well on the road to achieving this goal.”
Many new programs were begun that year. Increased
interest in Hebrew education enabled the Center to raise the
standards for Bar Mitzvah. In addition, Consecration for First
Grade of the Hebrew School and Kindergarten of the Sunday
School was held for the first time during Shemini Atzeret
evening services. The “Bas” Mitzvah ceremony was
introduced for girls of age 13. The first of many such
ceremonies took place on April 9,1948, when the congregation
hosted the Southeastern Regional United Synagogue
Conference. A champion of superior education for all students,
Ted Gross personally trained girls to become Bat Mitzvah.
The women in our congregation are, today, the beneficiaries
of his encouragement.
It was a hectic period for the new Education Director as
he added staff, supervised curricula and implemented new
programs; but he found time to give special attention to one
Sunday School teacher — Eunice Davis.
The Sunday School staff of 1948
===== PAGE 140 =====

===== PAGE 147 =====
— The Samuel & Esther Galinsky Educational Programs —
Early Childhood
Dale Schemer
Director
The Early Childhood Department of the Jacksonville Jewish Center is
entering its 49th year of providing quality programs to Jewish children in the
community, regardless of affiliation. Our ever expanding program offers not
only a Florida Kindergarten Council accredited preschool, but also includes an
extended day program available to all children enrolled in the Preschool and
Solomon Schechter Day School.
Our Preschool continues to offer the best secular and Judaic early childhood
program for children 12 months to 4 years of age.
This past year was a rewarding and exciting one. Our enrollment grew
and new programs were added, including computer classes for Nursery and
Pre-K students.
The Extended Day and Giant Steps programs saw a number of changes. New staff
was added, beginning with Cheril Clevette, our new program coordinator. Under her able
direction, the Extended Day Program provides outstanding before and after school care
with many new activities.
On behalf of the Preschool and Extended Day staff, I wish everyone a healthy and
happy New Year.
— Dale Schemer
Shirley Thacker
Secretary
Retirement Announcement
Ann Young retired this June after teaching for 28 years at the Center Preschool.
Ann has shaped the lives of hundreds of children with devotion, creative teaching and
affection. She has been a thoughtful co-worker, mentor to younger teachers, and a
good friend and advisor to parents of her Pre-Kindergarten students. Her students love
her for her winning smile, gentle guidance and genuine understanding. She will be
greatly missed and we wish her well in her retirement.

Youth Activities
Summer Programs for Jewish Youth
Camp Ramah Palmer and Ramah Darom
The Jacksonville Jewish Center is very fortunate to have a large representation
of youngsters participating in the Camp Ramah programs both in New England
and the new Ramah Darom in Georgia. Ramah, an arm of the Conservative
Movement, offers a wonderful summer opportunity for informal enrichment and
meaningful education.
Attending Camp Ramah Palmer in New England were: Ashley Osterer,
Melissa Osterer, Amy Schuster (not shown) and Hope Axelrod.
Attending Ramah Darom in Georgia were: Josh Appelbaum, Geri Bernard,
Jon Bernhardt, Susan Bernhardt, Aaron Blankstein, Sarah Blankstein, Sasha
Bloom, Robyn Blum, Leah Dubin, Jonathan Heller, Max Horovitz, Alison

tour together.
USY Israel/Poland Pilgrimage and
Ramah in Israel
This is a unique opportunity for
young people ages 15 to 18 to visit
Israel. Based in Jerusalem each of our
groups travels the country experiencing
their Jewish heritage. In addition to
spending a delightful summer with their
Israeli counterparts, our “pilgrims”
also develop lifelong friendships with
their traveling companions from the
United States and Canada. An additional
tour of Poland gives a deeper
understanding of the Holocaust. Center
USYers who went on Pilgrimage were
Justin Axelrod, Lauren Bloom,
Crista Cohen, Sam Horovitz, Sara
Mizrahi, Sean Pozin and Allison
Zisser.
Leadership Training Institute
Summer Encampment 2000
Summers are topped off with a
unique one-week experience held each
August. Teenagers participate in
programs that include informal classes
and discussion groups, cultural
activities and special evening activities
in addition to a full range of camp
sports and social activities. This year
Rachel Rosner attended LTI.
U.S.Y. on Wheels
This fine program gives teenagers an opportunity to travel
around the United States seeing landmarks, historical sites and
National parks. In addition they meet Jewish youth in the cities in
which they stay. This year Laney Cohen, Michael Demri, Debra

===== PAGE 150 =====
Lifecycle Events
Burial and Mourning
Center Cemetery
The Center owns and maintains two cemeteries adjacent to the
Evergreen Cemetery in North Jacksonville. Both are open daylight hours
every day except Shabbat and Jewish holidays. To reach the Old Cemetery,
travel north on North Main Street to Winona. Make a right on Winona and
go until you reach Gate 5. The Old Cemetery is on the left. To reach the
New Cemetery, travel north on North Main Street to 43rd Street. Make
a right on 43rd Street and the entrance
is at the next right, which is Liberty
Street.
This year, middle school students
of the Solomon Schechter Day School
learned, through the Mitzvah Program,
about the respectful care of the dead,
including tending of burial sites. On a
visit to the Old Cemetery, they discovered that several family plots no longer
had loved ones to maintain them. The students rolled up their sleeves and,
with great care and respect, cleaned the neglected headstones of a family
that been laid to rest more than 50 years ago. We are proud and grateful to
these children for performing an important mitzvah.
Future plans for the cemetery include improvements to the entrances,
as well as additional landscaping. Contributions can be made to the Cemetery
Fund in honor or in memory of loved ones. All donations will be used to
enhance and maintain our cemeteries.
We thank the volunteers
who serve on this
important committee:
Elyse Whitman, chairperson
Barbara Cantor
Charlotte Fialkow
Stacey Goldring
Dr. Jeffrey Goldstein
Stuart Hecht
Fred Kupperman
Leonardo Maiman

Students from Solomon Schechter Day
School’s Mitzvah Program cleaned
unattended headstones.
Hevra Kaddisha
Officers 2000-2001
President
Nathan C. Sandler
VP/Treasurer
Bob Bossen
VP/Education
Ira Grann
Taharah Committee Chairs
Use Gottlieb
Sally Becker
It is a source of pride and comfort for the entire Jewish community
that our Hevra Kaddisha is celebrating 30 years of dedicated service to the
dear departed. The burial society presently has 40 active members.
The concept of Hevra Kaddisha is based on kindness jj- not a reciprocal
type of kindness, but the true kindness of doing and caring for someone who
cannot return the favor. Our members perform these necessary services
because it is the right thing to do. Their satisfaction comes from knowing
that they are helping families at a time of grief and turmoil.
The Hevra Kaddisha is available 24 hours a day to perform the Tahara
(purification) rituals for cleansing and preparing the body for burial; to recite
the traditional prayers and to shroud the body in white linen, Tacrichim; and
to provide a Shomer (watchman) to remain with the body until burial. Families
can take comfort knowing that members of the Hevra Kaddisha are well
trained in the traditional duties, and are devoted to showing the utmost respect
for the deceased.
VP/Secretary
Naomie Bossen
The Jewish community, regardless of affiliation, is encouraged to call
and discuss their concerns with any of our officers, as well as the rabbis.
Dedication is our watchword.
—Nathan C. Sandler, president

Community Organizations
Hadassah
National Council of Jewish Women
“Hadassah has always been an important bridge to
peace. By treating all people without regard to nationality or
religion—Hadassah has shown the world what peace in the
Middle East will look like.” -Yitzchak Rabin, Jerusalem, 1994.
Judaism teaches that it is not enough to avoid iniquity
— we must actively pursue righteousness and justice at home,
in the, community, and in the world. In this tradition, Hadassah
was founded in 1912 by Henrietta Szold to bring public health
services to pre-state Israel. Today, more than 300,000
American women support our network of Israel projects in
addition to our volunteer work at home. Across the US,
Hadassah promotes health education, community service, and
Jewish education and research. Hadassah advocates on
issues ranging from Israel-US relations to First Amendment
protections to women’s rights and health concerns.
One by one, we must each take responsibility for
transforming hopes, promises, and echoes into deeds.
Jacksonville Hadassah invites your participation in one of
our five groups: Hannah Senesch, Shir Li, Tikva, Nurse’s &
HCP Council and Yamit.
For information please contact any of our presidents:
Chapter
Hannah Senesch
Nurses & HCP Council

Phyllis Goldberg
The National Council of Jewish Women (NCJW) is a
volunteer organization, inspired by Jewish values, that works
through a program of research, education, advocacy, and
community service to improve the quality of life for women,
children and families, and strives to ensure individual rights
and freedoms for all.
The Jacksonville section of NCJW was established in
1939, and is currently involved in such programs as:
1. Organizing forums for candidates for local offices to
present their views to the Jewish community;
2. Bringing kosher meals, as well as a caring word, to
homebound Jewish people;
3. Organizing advocacy on state and federal issues
involving woman, children and families;
4. Providing a Hanukkah celebration at Wolfson’s Children’s
Hospital, bringing entertainment and gifts to patients;
5. Registering voters as part of a national “Promote the
Vote” campaign;
6. Providing entertainment and refreshments to Mt.
Carmel residents;
7. Participating in Israeli society through a variety of
education-oriented projects;
8. Recognizing women who have made great contributions
to our community, through our annual Women in Power
Luncheon;^
9. Continued support of programs which we helped start, and
which now function independently, such as Guardian Ad Litem,
Home Instruction Program for Preschool Youngsters and PACE.
For information, contact Gloria Einstein or
the NCJW Message Line — 443-2820

Religious Schools
Abraham Joshua Heschel Leadership Group
This year the Jacksonville Jewish Center formed the Abraham Joshua Heschel Leadership
Group guided by Rabbi David Gaffney and Rabbi Dov Kentof. This unique group is made up of 43
Jewish teenagers who are serious about their religion and intent upon taking an active leadership role in
the synagogue and the community.
Through discussion groups, guest speakers, services, and other programs centered on leadership
themes, this group of young people takes positive steps towards their goals. The group involves itself in
serious issues and has become the core of leadership for the Center’s youth.
Among its activities this year, the
Heschel Group organized food
drives, hosted an outing for the
Russian/American community
and observed Havdalah and
holidays together.
The Heschel Group held a leadership seminar with representatives of the major Jewish agencies
College Outreach
Through special mailings, the
Education and Youth Department keeps our
college students up-to-date on what’s going
on back home, as well as informed of Jewish
issues around the world. Seasonal packages
also contain holiday treats. In addition, Rabbi
David Gaffney meets with students of the
University of Florida at the campus Hillel,
every year, to help keep them connected. If
you would like your college student included
in this program, contact Stella Finck, who
maintains the mailing list and facilitates the
mailings.

Sunday Sports - Basketball Program
The Sunday Sports Association (SSA) provides area youth with alternative
athletic programs on Sunday afternoons. All the games and practices are held in the
Fletcher-Selber Auditorium of the Jacksonville Jewish Center. Thank you to Gayle
Bailys who coordinated a very successful program and to the volunteer coaches for
their valuable assistance and time. We look forward to an exciting 200-2001season.

Every Issue Is Worth Getting Into.
The Lifestyle section of The Florida Times-
Union is a great way to find out what’s
going on around town or even in
your own back yard. With features
about gardening, home projects
and health and fitness, the
Lifestyle section covers issues that
you can relate to. Plus, there’s always
great articles about local people, events
and stories that make Jacksonville such a
great place to live. And be sure to check out
the special Friday "Lifestyle” issue for the
inside scoop about local hot spots, movies and
special events. So keep up with life in
Jacksonville by reading the Lifestyle section of
the T-U every day.
