President’s Message
As the newly installed President of
the Jacksonville Jewish Center, there are
no words to describe my excitement for
the coming year. We are facing many
challenges on the horizon, including the
beginning of an extensive and arduous
search for new Rabbinical leadership; the
implementation of our Restoration 2000
project; and the continued development and
growth of our outstanding Galinsky
Educational Programs - just to name a few!
Michael Shorstein
President
Perhaps you enjoy outdoor,
recreational excursions - become a
member of our Summer Recreation
Program! Go white water rafting with
Rabbi Kentof, fishing with the Men’s
Club, or participate in our JJC Golf
Classic.
Anywhere your interests may lie,
there are exciting opportunities waiting for
you!
My objective as president is to ensure that in all the
transitions and changes we make, we will strive for
excellence. This “Initiative for Excellence” needs to touch
all aspects of our lives at the Center - from our Galinsky
Educational Programs, Religious experiences and
Congregational Programming, to our leadership, staff and
membership participation.
We need to work together in this journey for
excellence, because it is only through teamwork, joint
effort and common goals that it is attainable. Join and
participate in one of our many committees dedicated to
planning and providing creative programming for all
aspects of the Center.
If your interests lean toward adult-oriented activities,
join our Sisterhood or Men’s Club, take an adult education
class, attend our Shabbaton or one of our Performing
Artist’s Series shows. They are yours, just for the taking.
If you are interested in the continued growth of the
Center, check out our newly redesigned Membership
committee and sub-committees.
We must remember that the true reason we work
so diligently is to instill enthusiasm in the youth of our
congregation. Our youth are the future of our synagogue
and of our community. We must set an example for
them. How we focus on our Jewish heritage, community
and responsibilities will teach them that the Center, and
this community, are their future!
I invite you to join us as we embark on our journey,
into the second centennial of the Jacksonville Jewish
Center.
On a more personal level, I would like to thank
Rabbi Gaffney for his 29 years of leadership, guidance
and commitment to our synagogue. I have shared so many
life cycle events with both the Rabbi and Inge; their
friendship and devotion will always be remembered and
cherished.
On behalf of Robin, Mathew, Benay and myself,
L’Shana Tova from my family to yours!
— Michael
Berman Bros., Inc.
Best Wishes for a
J

Community Agencies
River (¡ügíp|)) Garden
HEBREW HOME/WOLFSON HEALTH & AGING CENTER
11401 Old St. Augustine Road • 260-9020 • www.rivergarden.org
“Eldercare At Its Best”
_“Honor thy father and mother that thy days may be long . . .” It was this
commandment which inspired the founding of River Garden Hebrew Home in
1946. It was this commandment which nourished the love and care that for more
than fifty years has made River Garden a nationally recognized model of
excellence in its field. It was this commandment that made it necessary to create
a Home that is welcoming to families and encourages its use as an extension of
family space. River Garden residents are a part of the community, not apart from it!
The River Garden Hebrew Home has also become the anchor of a growing
system of elder services including the Home, The Coves, Family Care Support
program and Home Health Agency. The success of River Garden is based on the
tradition of meeting 100 percent of local Jewish community needs and of serving
rich and poor alike with excellence. The River Garden Foundation accepts
donations to help River Garden continue to meet its mission. This would not be
possible without substantial charitable support from the community and the work
of The River Garden Foundation to stimulate planned gift annuities, trusts and
bequests.
River Garden’s programs of short-term rehabilitative/respite care, long¬
term residential care, Alzheimers’ and Adult Day Care, serve over 180 people
on any given day. These programs are guided by a devoted, professional full
time staff of over 200. Staff includes physicians and beauticians; nurses, social
workers, pharmacists, activities specialists; physical occupational and speech
therapists; dieticians, etc. In addition, scores of dedicated volunteers help create
a special caring community.
Located on a 35 acre Mandarin campus containing lush Florida oak and
pine trees, a private lake, meandering walking paths, River Garden is the perfect
setting for residents and visitors. River Garden is a community where people
live, love and care; a community of many lifestyles and of rich Jewish content,
and a community which every day strives to live up to the mandate of the Fifth
Commandment.
In recent years, life on campus has become more active and attractive with
the completion of The Coves, the elegant, affordable retirement community.
River Garden
FOUNDATION

Now in its sixth year, this elegant
yet affordable retirement community is
located on River Garden’s 35 acre
campus in Mandarin.
Sponsored by the not-for-profit
River Garden Holding Company, The
Coves offers comfort, security, club¬
house living and the opportunity for
continued growth during the retirement
years in a Jewishly sponsored
envronment.
The River Garden Foundation is a philanthropic organization, established
to provide resources for programs and facilities to enhance the quality of life for
the aged. Its primary purpose is to fund the not-for-profit River Garden system of
services.
The foundation is dedicated to helping the elderly remain in control of their
own lives by assuring services to people at all levels of need and financial ability.
The aim of the Foundation is to keep pace with the changing needs of the
aging through programs that meet a broad array of health care needs, as well as
provide a full spectrum of residential options.

Center Choral Society

For over 53 years, the Center Choir has been enhancing services
on the High Holidays and Shavuot with moving liturgical music. Over
the years they have given numerous concerts featuring members of the
choir as well as nationally acclaimed soloists. Many of the current
members have been singing with this group for twenty years or more.
New members are always welcome. Call Pollie Copans, 731-5980.
Center Havurot
A Havurah is a small group of congregation members
(families, couples, singles) who meet regularly for activities or
experiences of their mutual choosing. The groups are varied but
all gather together to enjoy life as Jews through socializing,
education, discussion of Jewish issues, worship or sharing of
Jewish holidays and lifecycle celebrations.
A Havurah provides an extended family for those who have
relocated to Jacksonville, as well as a supportive group of friends
for those whose family composition has changed.
There are currently five Havurot associated with our
synagogue. The oldest group formed in 1974 and is still meeting.
Others boast that members who have moved away still come back
to Jacksonville for holidays and simchas.
If you would like to become part of a Havurah, call Stella
Finck, 292-0914, or the Center office, 292-1000.
Children in their “Havurah” tee shirts gathered on Sukkot at the home
of Barbara and Eliot Safer, in 1988. They still do!
Jewish Singles
Another year of activities has passed for the Jewish singles of Jacksonville. Dinner continues to be a favorite pastime,
but brunch, holiday parties and a few day trips have also been scheduled. Touring the San Sebastian Winery was a highlight of
the past year’s activities.
Singles get-togethers are great for forming friendships, networking and romance. This past year, at least four couples
met and three weddings are already scheduled.
Calendars of events are mailed several times a year, and e-mail has proven to be helpful in keeping in touch as well.
This group is open to any Jewish single, age 24ish to 45ish, in the Jacksonville area. For more information, or to be put
on the mailing list, call Rhoda at the Center office, 292- 1000.

Center Youth Groups
Research has proven that the survival of Judaism depends on the exposure of our youth to Jewish activities, friends and
experiences that commit them to perpetuating that feeling of Jewishness and Jewish life.
The Jacksonville Jewish Center sponsors three outstanding youth groups for youngsters in grades 4-12. Each group
meets regularly and enjoys programs of a religious, cultural and social nature.
Through active participation in these groups, a sense of pride and an identification with Judaism are instilled. Jewish
values, attitude and behavior patterns are discussed and carried out through Mitzvah programs and study.
Conventions, regional activities and camps give our youth the opportunity to meet other Jewish youth from all over the
United States.
The youth programs are coordinated by Rabbi Dov Kentof, and are supervised by the Youth Commission. All groups
are affiliated with the Southeast Region and United Synagogue of America.

Scouting
Boy Scout Troop 14
Troop 14 continued the scouting tradition at the
Jacksonville Jewish Center with another year of outdoor
fun, adventure and activities in 1999-2000. Bob Fleet
served as Scoutmaster, and was assisted by Assistant
Scoutmasters Louis Schwartz and
Billy Wilensky. Youth leadership
was provided by Justin Jackral,
Junior Assistant Scoutmaster, Jared
Fleet, Senior Patrol Leader, and
Michael Demri, Assistant Senior
Patrol Leader.
This year, the troop went on
campouts to Goldhead Branch State
Park, Laura Walker State Park near
Waycross, Georgia, Florida Caverns State Park near
Marianna, where they enjoyed spelunking. The trip to
Skidaway Island Sate Park in Savannah, Georgia, was
especially exciting. One half of the scouts traveled to
Skidaway Island on Amtrak, and the other half traveled
back in a stretch limousine.
Other activities the scouts enjoyed included laser
tag, go-kart racing, playing miniature golf, and attending
the Jacksonville Suns Opening Game.
Once again, the scouts purchased food for the Food
Bank for Thanksgiving. They also donated prizes they
earned from selling Entertainment Books to the Day
School’s “adopted” holiday families.
A lot of scouts made strides
in advancement this year. Leonard
Beir became the most recent
member of Troop 14 to earn Boy
Scouting’s highest honor, the rank
of Eagle. Fourteen scouts attended
summer camp with Troop 14 at
Camp Grimes in North Carolina.
They were led by Assistant
Scoutmaster Louis Schwartz.
Troop 14 looks forward to continuing its proud
tradition of providing Jewish youth with a Boy Scouting
experience. If you enjoy camping, sports, a variety of
outdoor activities, and are between the ages of 11 and
18, we invite you to come to our meetings at the Center
on Thursday nights. The troop also welcomes participation
from adults interested in providing volunteer assistance.
For more information call Bob Fleet at (H) 268-2746
or (W)730-8103.
Check out that gator!
Scouts cut wood for a campfire.
Part of the Troop traveled to a campout
aboard Amtrak.

A Message from Rabbi Gaffney
A Resume for the Soul
One of the effects which the
yamim mora ’im - the Days of Awe have
upon the mind of the Jew is the acute
awareness of the passing of time. We
look back and comment on how quickly
the old year has passed and we
contemplate, sometimes anxiously, the
year which lies ahead. In our prayers
we ask to be inscribed in God’s book
for a good life. We Jews take the
passage of time very seriously. We
invoke the name of God when we recite
the blessing of Shehicheyanu, —
“...Who has kept us in life and enabled
us to celebrate this moment in time.”
We read with the psalmist every Shabbat
-“so teach us to number our days that
we may get us a heart of wisdom.”
Abraham Joshua Heschel, one of our
most profound thinkers, has described
the importance of celebrating Shabbat
and holidays by suggesting that Jews
never build shrines in space ...rather they
fashioned sanctuaries in time.
We mark the passages of time, the
transition of the year 5760 to 5761 by
suggesting that it be accompanied by a
sober assessment of how we are
spending our time...by heshbon
ha’nefesh, by reflecting and
contemplating our spiritual journey
...literally, by an “accounting of the
soul”. The passage of time, in a word,
elicits sobriety and solemnity. Time is
after all our most priceless possession.
This year, especially, I am
prompted to such personal
considerations. After almost thirty
years I will be welcoming, dear friends,
along with you a successor who will
hopefully serve the Jacksonville Jewish
Center with as much satisfaction with
which I have served over these many
years. It is a time for transition, dear
friends, for me and for you.
I remember still the résumé that I
forwarded to leaders of the
congregation in May of 1972. It
detailed the formalities that are typical
in résumés in any profession. I listed
the schools I attended, where I received
my rabbinical degree, the colleges and
university in which I earned my
bachelors and masters degree, the
academic honors that I received and the
professional organizations with which
I was associated.
Rabbi David and Inge Gaffney
This résumé did not convey, as no
résumé could, the essence of my life.
Let me explain. When I meet with a
family to discuss the celebration of a
bar or bat mitzvah my concern is not
only the number of Torah honors that
will be distributed; the number of verses
the young celebrant will chant or what
the theme of the bar mitzvah party is. I
want to know something about the life
of the young man or woman. Is he or
she aware of the magnitude and
importance of this rite of passage? Does
the bar mitzvah know that all of Jewish
history is attending his celebration?
And what about the personal life of the
bat mitzvah? What is important to her
and what gives her life meaning?
When I attempt to help a family
to cope with the passing of a loved one
as we discuss funeral arrangements I try
to evoke something that goes beyond
information found in the obituary
column. I attempt to ascertain more
than the years that their loved one lived
or the names of the organizations to
which they belonged. My hope is to
elicit the essence of a person’s life, to
speak about their relationships and to
discuss their feelings. I want the
résumé, as it were, but I hope for so
much more.
The résumé I submitted some
thirty years ago is much simpler than
the heshbon ha’nefesh...the accounting
of a rabbinic soul which I might compile
after thirty years. This résumé is much
more nuanced; much more complicated
than the résumé I submitted upon my
arrival. Have I touched someone’s soul?
Have I inspired someone to lead a more
meaningful Jewish life? Have I changed
someone’s heart or someone’s outlook
with a sermon? Did I provide some
insight with an interpretation of some
classic Jewish text? Has someone in a
class looked at things differently
because of the time we spent together?
Have I been faithful to God? Persistent
in my belief and faithful in my devotion?
Did I make a difference in someone’s
life? Did I help someone in a moment
of need? Did I induce real inner joy at a
simcha? Did I comfort a family in their
moment of grief?
These issues, dear friends, do not
appear in a résumé but are at the heart
of my heshbon ha’nefesh...iht
accounting of my soul. I have to date
not counted the number of baby namings
and b’nai mitzvah, weddings or funerals
at which I officiated. I have not taken a
sum total of the hours that I have spent
in preparing for classes or for sermons.
I suppose I could write a resume of this
sort of the last thirty years and provide
the data ...but this exercise could never
account for the really important issues
of my rabbinic life.
And then, dear friends, how about
you? We all write our own heshbon
ha’nefesh, our own résumé at different
and critical moments of our life. This
Rosh Hashanah should prompt you to
considerations of your own. What kind
of a husband have I been? Wife?
Parent? Child? Was I a sensitive
person? Did I give tzedakah? Did I care
about someone other than myself? How
did I answer the important questions of
life...not what I gained, but what I
gave...not what my station is, but what
have I become? The statistics say ...I
am a Jew -that is just data. More
important, what kind of a Jew have I
become and what have I done for the
Jewish people.
Make up your own résumé during
this season of transitions since for all
of us this is a time for heshbon
ha’nefesh—for reviewing the résumé
of our soul. It is perhaps the most
important endeavor we might undertake
-for me and for you.
Inge and I wish you and yours a
most meaningful Yom Tov. May the new
year bring all of us health, happiness,
fulfillment and peace. Amen

The Samuel & Esther Galinsky Educational Programs —
Religious Schools
Sunday School
The SUNDAY SCHOOL of the Jacksonville Jewish Center is
planned expressly for children in kindergarten, first and second grades.
A weekly, two-hour program gives each child the opportunity to
experience the richness of his/her Jewish heritage through song,
dance, role playing, cooking, short stories, games, arts and crafts.
Emphasis is placed on the holidays and festivals. Jewish values and
mitzvot are encouraged. Many thanks to our wonderful Sunday
School teachers Susan Kadish and Susan Neadle.
Students included Sarah Abramson, Cory Brenenson, Rachel
Cain, Lauren Greenspan, Madison Kress, Sarah Neadle, Alex Nield,
Jenny Nield, Benjamin Peltz, Rebecca Peltz, Joshua Peretzman, Ariella
Phillips, Harrison Safer and Daniel Udell.
Purim at Sunday School.
Religious Schools PTA
Youth Congregations
We are looking forward to another exciting year with
our Afternoon Hebrew, Sunday School and Beit Midrash
classes.

Kindergarten-2nd Grade
Meets Saturdays, lla.m.-Noon
Our younger students seem to become more involved
each year wjth our Jewish Holidays. They love performing in
programs for Passover and Purim. Our older students are
becoming serious, committed Jews.
Junior Congregation
Grades 3-6
Meets Saturdays, 10:45 a.m.-Noon
Saturday morning classes are taught before services
by Wendy Brezin, Suzy Kadish, Alina Kentof and
Susan Neadle.
Parental involvement is so very important in a child’s
religious education. Volunteers are always needed, and we
believe your children benefit from seeing you helping out.
Please feel free to volunteer whenever you are able, showing
your support for our programs.
Wishing you a wonderful and healthy New Year!

Community Organizations
American Red Magen David for Israel
Founded in 1930 as a First Aid Society, Magen David
Adorn has become the State of Israel’s emergency medical,
disaster, ambulance and healthcare network. 365 days a year,
24 hours a day, every person in every corner of Israel looks to
Magen David Adorn to perform the usual tasks carried out by
Red Cross Societies throughout the world. Within minutes,
MDA's rescue units arrive on the scene for medical
emergencies, accidents and, unfortunately, terrorist bombings.
Trained paramedics administer immediate help, and then
transport the patient to the hospital if necessary.
Mitzvah Chapter’s Annual Raffle proceeds help support
a cardiac ambulance for the city of Ashdod.
Even though the symbol of Magen David Adorn, a red
Star of David, is recognized by the American Red Cross, efforts
are still going on to achieve international acceptance of our
symbol.
As part of our continuing efforts to raise every possible
dollar, we have arranged for anyone whp can, to donate their
car, van, motorhome or boat—running or not!—to benefit
ARMDI. Its fully tax deductible. Call (800) 550-3333 and
mention ARMDI for details and/or pickup.
Show your support for the State of Israel for only $18
(chai - life), and do the mitzvah of pikkuach nefesh by joining
today. Mail to: Lea Gabby, 3068 Haley Lane, Jax.,FL 32257.
“For us it’s only a check, for them it could mean life itself.”

Brandéis University
National Women’s Committee
The mission of the Brandéis University National
Women’s Committee is to provide financial support and
growth for the Brandéis University Libraries, which serve a
community of students and scholars, in education and
research, united by their commitment to the pursuit of
knowledge. The National Women’s Committee offers its
members opportunity for intellectual pursuit, continuing
education, community service, social interaction, personal
enrichment, and leadership development. The members act
as emissaries to support and enhance the image of Brandéis,
a Jewish-sponsored, non-sectarian university where
excellence is the tradition.
For more information, call Betsy Pearl, 645-5410.

Solomon Schechter Day School
Day School/PreSchool PTA
i- 2000-2001 Officers -i
President
Meryl Rittenberg
Fundraising VP
Suzanne Weiss
Membership VP
Jeanine Rogozinski
Programming VP
Kim Schemer
Secretary
Helen DuBow
Treasurer
Sue Levine
Pre-School Liaison
Debbie Ring
The parents, teachers and administrators of the Solomon Schechter Day School and Pro¬
school work together to enhance the close knit nature of our schools, raise most needed funds
for school projects, and enlist the help of parent volunteers for a variety of programs. These
programs are made possible through our fundraising projects such as magazine sale, book fair,
and Passover candy sales. Active membership allows many opportunities to make a lasting
contribution to the students and the school, as well as developing long lasting relationships
with other parents and members of the Schechter family. Our volunteers are truly dedicated to
the children in providing quality programs throughout the year.
This past year, PTA provided the schools with lab equipment for the newly adopted
science program for grades one through seven, as well as educational computer programs,
library books, video catalog note cards, music books and supplies for the Day School. For the
Preschool, we furnished special area rugs to brighten the classrooms, safety I.D. wristbands
for field trips, a six-seat baby buggy and much more.
Some of the educational and enrichment programs we provide are: Holiday observances
such as Shabbat boxes, weekly Challah orders, helping with the celebration of Rosh Hashanah,
Chanukah, Purim and Passover model Seders; Kaleidoscope Cultural Arts Day; Red Ribbon
Week for drug awareness; Vision Screening; Library Assistants; Picture Lady and Mystery
Reader; introducing art appreciation and storytelling programs for Pre-kindergarten,
Kindergarten and First Grade.
We appreciate your commitment to the PTA. Whether you volunteer your time or give your financial support, the result is
always a successful educational experience for our children.
L’ShanaTovah,
—Meryl Rittenberg
1999-2000 Solomon Schechter Day School Teachers and Staff

Scouting
Cub Scout Pack 14
Cub Scout Pack 14 enjoyed a great
year! We broke records by going on three
camp outs with great participation from our
Pack Family. Pack 14 was seen camping at
the Suwannee River, the Olustee Battlefield
Reenactment and right in our own back yard
at the Center.
We congratulate our WeBeLos who
moved up to the Boy Scout Troop 14.
Among our activities, the annual
Pinewood Derby drew our Pack’s families
together for a morning of racing competition and family fun
at River Garden. Our dens also learned about nature, safety,
community and Judaism.
We are proud of our new den, the Tiger Cubs. A big
Scout salute to the first-grade Tiger Cub Program, now in
its second year at the Center. Tiger Cubs is geared towards
boys in the first grade, whereas traditional Cub Scouting
begins in the second grade.
We extend our sincerest thanks
to Cubmaster Jim Richman, as he
retires as leader of Pack 14 for eight
years! He has lead a proud pack, one of
the oldest in Florida! We welcome
Bruce Goldring, our new Cubmaster,
and look forward to more great
experiences under his leadership.
We also thank Stacy Epstein who
has been involved in den leadership for
six years, one of which she volunteered
as den leader for both of her sons’ dens. We are grateful to
our den leaders: Stacy Epstein; Kim Gartner; Jeri
Schwartz and Elissa Vining and all our volunteer parents who
have committed their valuable time to our children, the Cub
Scouts of Mighty Mighty Pack 14!
For more information on Cub Scouting, call any of our
den leaders, or Cubmaster, Bruce Goldring at 739-2970.
Cubmasters Bruce Goldring and Jim

Special Events
Simhat Torah Honorees
The High Holiday season reaches its joyous climax on Simhat Torah, the last day of the festival
of Sukkot. Because of our perennial love of the Torah, it has been referred to as Israel’s “bride”. On
Simhat Torah, we bring to a close the annual cycle of the reading of the Torah and immediately begin
anew. An ancient tradition evolved of honoring worthy men by calling them to the Torah for the last
reading, Hatan Torah, and the beginning portion, Hatan Bereshit. In our synagogue tradition, we
also honor the contributions made by a “Woman of Valor”.
Philip Bloom Michael Shorstein Bonnie Sandler
Hatan Torah Hatan Bereshit Woman of Valor
Philip is a man of
few words, but of
many virtues.
Concern for others,
strong ethical and
family value, the
importance of
Jewish education
and tzedakah, are
principles that our Hatan Torah has put
into action for the betterment of our
congregation. During the threat of
Hurricane Floyd, while others attended
to personal preparations, Philip was at
the Center making sure the Torahs were
secure. He is a regular at the morning
minyans and Rabbi Gaffney’s Sunday
morning Talmud class.
Philip has served on the Board of
Directors for three years in the capacity
of chairman of the House Committee.
Currently he is an Executive Board
member and also serves on the Finance
Committee. As house committee
chairman, Philip spearheaded the efforts
of the 2001 Centennial Challenge
Campaign, which provided handicapped
access to the bima, major kitchen
renovations, a refurbished pool and
recreation park, new air conditioning
and rest rooms for our schools and a new
energy management system to govern
our facility. Under his direction, a new,
sophisticated security system was
installed.
Philip is a successful building
contractor whose expertise is vital to the
new Restoration 2000 Project.
His talent, creativity and
dedication have been of great value to
the Jacksonville Jewish Center. It is with
much appreciation that the Jacksonville
Jewish Center honored Philip Bloom as
Hatan Torah.
Mazel Tov to him, his wife Linda,
daughters, Lauren and Sasha and family
and friends who shared in this special
honor.
Michael epitomizes
the talented “ home
grown” leaders who
devote their time
and energy to the
Center. It is a
family legacy. His
father, Jack and
brother, Mark, both
served as the synagogue’s president.
Now, Michael is our newest president.
Growing up, Michael attended
Solomon Schechter Day School and was
active in Jewish youth groups at the Center.
He has a degree in accounting from the
University of Florida and his law degree
from Florida State. Michael is also a CPA.
Michael served as Firfct Vice-
President and chairman of the Center’s
Finance Committee, a member of the
Board and Executive Committee and
played a major role in fundraising and
educational efforts, such as the new JJC
Golf Classic.
When called upon to take on many of
the synagogue’s more demanding issues,
Michael handled the responsibilities with his
own unique style of humor and
determination. Through his leadership, the
Finance committee worked diligently to
improve the synagogue’s financial situation,
resulting in the retirement of the Center’s
mortgage this year.
Michael is also very active in the
community. As an attorney specializing
in adoption law, he works closely with
JFCS and volunteers countless hours of
free consultation in the area of family
adoption. Michael has also recently
served as chairman of the Judicial
Nominating Commission of the Fourth
Judicial Circuit. As with so many other
“Center trained” volunteers, Michael is
frequently called upon to daven at
religious services.
Michael shared this honor with his
wife Robin, and children, Mathew and
Benay.
Bonnie truly fits
the description of a
Woman of Valor.
She has a warm,
winning smile, and
a sweet gentle
nature that endears
her to everyone she
meets. She is a soft-
spoken leader who attracts and inspires
others to join in her worthy endeavors.
She is clever and intelligent, but modest
about her accomplishments. She is a
devoted wife, mother, daughter, vital
synagogue leader, respected teacher and
a caring community member.
Shortly after moving here from New
York, Bonnie and husband Neil became
co-presidents of the Center’s newly
formed young couples club and were
soon helping newer members to establish
Jewish roots and new friendships at the
Center. With a degree in Math Education
from Brooklyn College, Bonnie began
tutoring children in her home, which
enabled her to volunteer at the
synagogue and in the community.
Over the years, Bonnie held
numerous positions in the Center
Sisterhood. She served as president from
1996-1998, presided as hostess of Spring
Branch Conference, and is currently area
coordinator for Florida Branch of
Women’s League for Conservative
Judaism. In addition, Bonnie has been a
long time member of Hadassah and
National Council of Jewish Women.
An active Center Board member
for over 20 years, Bonnie served on the
Education and Membership committees,
and was Membership co-chair for several
terms. She prides herself on continuing
her own Jewish education as a member
of the Sisterhood B’nai Mitzvah Class of
1990.
Bonnie shared this simcha with her
husband, Neil, children, Scott, Laurie and
Paul.

Youth Activities
White Water Rafting Experience
Led by Rabbi Dov Kentof
As always, this year’s White Water Rafting Trip was FANTASTIC! As in the past,
two rivers were explored: the Nolichucky and the French Broad. Everyone had a blast,
and made it home with all their body parts intact!
In addition, participants camped, held discussion groups, went tubing and prayed
in beautiful country settings. The memories made on this trip will last a lifetime, and
strengthen Judaism for these participants, in a unique way.
Jewish Community Programs for Youth
This year Rabbi Dov Kentof applied his talents to two community activity days sponsored by the Jacksonville Jewish
Educators Council and the Jacksonville Jewish Federation. Building on programs presented by our Family Council, Rabbi
Kentof was able to bring the same high quality activities to the entire Jewish community.
Families boarded “Noah's Ark” for a re-creation of his journey. Then visited Noah's tent, fed his
animals, learned about ancient life and even rode a camel.
The Community Field Day brought kids
together for athletic activities.

Shabbat Greeters
Martha Savage, Chairperson
Martha Savage coordinates the
friendly volunteers who give of their time
to perform the mitzvah of welcoming
people to service/S with a friendly
“Shabbat Shalom”. Greeting is a good
way to introduce yourself to people and
make newcomers and visitors feel
welcome. We thank Martha for her
dedication to the Center and to all of the people who volunteered to greet over the
past year. Anyone interested in joining the Shabbat Greeters, please call Martha,
733-4668.

Henry Kramer Library and Resource Center
Minnie Schreiber and May Goldie Stillman, Chairs
Did you know that you can enjoy the Forward newspaper or Moment Magazine
right in the Center library? Current journals and magazines are available in the quiet,
comfortable setting of the Tofield Reading Room of the Henry Kramer Library. The
collection of Judaica contains reference books on the Bible, prayer, customs and
rituals, art, history and the Holocaust. The Steinsaltz Talmud in Hebrew and English
is available, and reference materials are accessible for study assignments. There are
books on philosophy, Israel, music and cooking. You will find popular novels, poetry
and books of Jewish humor.
Visit the Henry Kramer Library on Sundays 9:00 to noon. It’s your library.
Shabbat Torah Readers
Ted Gross, Coordinator
Half a century seems like a very
long time to achieve a goal for the
special activities in which I have
participated; but, when it comes to the
word of God, there is no limitation
imposed.
Of all the outstanding areas in
which the Jacksonville Jewish Center
has excelled, it seems that we have been
most fortunate in being favored with
people who have made their talents
meaningful to the congregation and a
source of recognition and pride
throughout the Southeast. The numbers
of students and lay people who can be
depended upon to read Torah, even on
short notice, would be very hard to
match by other synagogues. This is a
reflection of three things: skilled reading
ability, mastery of the trope and the
dedication of our readers. I am very
proud to be associated with the Torah
reading program, which continues to keep
the Center on a high level. The knowledge,
commitment and encouragement of
synagogue leaders will ensure that this
high quality will be maintained in the
future. Mazel tov to all of you,
readers and teachers. You have
discovered a treasure, and give us all
nachas when you share it with us.
- Library Committee -

Organizations
Men’s Club Man of the Year Banquet
One evening last October, Neil Sandler
was teased, taunted, harassed and embarrassed
by some of his closest friends. The “Roast of
New York” honored Neil as the Center Men’s
Club Man of the Year. No one is more
deserving of this title. Neil distinguished
himself, and made the Men’s Club a valuable
asset to the synagogue, by developing
programs and events of interest to men and
to benefit the youth of our congregation. As
the second president of the organization in
1992-93, he often single-handedly planned
and executed monthly meetings. By
consistently volunteering the Men’s Club for
all kinds of jobs around the congregation, Neil
drew great attention to the fledgling organization which he
helped to establish. Today the Men’s Club is a well-respected
and valued part of the Jacksonville Jewish Center, due in no
small measure to the efforts of Neil Sandler.
Michael Shorstein was emcee
extraordinaire of the unbelievable “adults
only” evening filled with friendly toasts and
roasts and some surprises. In addition to the
planned program, banquet-goers paid for an
on-the-spot opportunity to say a few words
about Neil. The results were hilarious. The
wonderful evening included a Coney Island,
N.Y., boardwalk-style menu. Thanks to Ellen
Rubens for creating a delightful ambiance.
All proceeds went to benefit the Men’s
Club Summer Scholarship Fund for needy
Jewish youth, which was named this year in
loving memory of Horty Gendzier.
The response to this gala evening was overwhelming.
Make your plans to attend this year’s fun-filled event when
another outstanding man will be honored.
Men's Club President Dave
Schmerer presented award to Neil
Sandler.
Emcee Michael Shorstein Bonnie Sandler revealed some “fishy” tibits about
doin' his thing! hubby Neil.
The Setzer Social Hall was packed, and. a great time was had by all.
Yad Shel Chai recipients Crista Cohen andAvi Richman.
Yad Shel Chai Award
Among it’s many activities, the Jacksonville Jewish Center Men’s
Club promotes positive youth programs. The Men’s Club instituted the
very successful Yad Shel Chai (Hand of Life) award program to encourage
and reward post Bar/Bat Mitzvahs who continue reading Torah on
Shabbat, holidays, and at minyan. Teens who read a minimum of 18
(chai) portions by age 18 are awarded a beautiful, inscribed Torah pointer
(yad). Over two dozen teens have already received this award, and
many more are are currently enrolled in the program. At Men’s Club
Shabbat, this past year, Crista Cohen, Daniel Passen and Avi Richman
received a yad for reaching this important goal. We should all be extremely
proud of their accomplishments and hope to see many more join them in
achieving this high honor. If you would like more information regarding
this program, please contact Randall Smith or Jim Richman.

Committees
Daily Minyan Captains
Traditionally, public worship requires a minyan, a
quorum of ten. Only in the presence of a minyan may the
Torah be read or the Kaddish prayer be recited.
Our dedicated minyan captains ensure that there is a
minyan twice every single day of the year. It is often a hard
and thankless job. It requires hours of phoning to coordinate
attendance.
It is because of them that you can recite kaddish when
you mourn or observe yarhzeit. We owe the captains not
only our thanks, but also our participation, in order to
continue providing a minyan for each service. Please call
any minyan captain and become a “regular” for at least one
minyan a week.

Shabbat/Holiday Ushers
Fred Blum & Tom Spriggs, Chairs
Every Shabbat and holidays these friendly volunteer
members serve as ambassadors to Center congregants by helping
with seating, guiding and acknowledging newcomers, and
welcoming regular worshippers. Ushers help to maintain
synagogue decorum which preserves the beauty of the service
for all of us. We thank all of our ushers for their efforts throughout
the year:

Membership
Phyllis Goldberg, Chairperson
Rhoda Goldstein and Judy Greenfield
prepare welcome bags.
As we begin the new century, the membership committee
continues to focus its efforts on promoting the well-being
and growth of the membership of the Jacksonville Jewish
Center. Helping newcomers to the community become a part
of our Center “family”is our main purpose.
We understand the importance of giving those who
relocate to Jacksonville a support system — a place for people
to make friends and find an extended family.
The Jacksonville Jewish Center provides a place for
socialization and recreation, as well as a place for religious
services and Jewish educational programs. We attract new
members, and retain those who have already joined us, by
providing for their needs. The members of the membership
committee, and indeed all members of the congregation, are
an important part of this process.
You can help us accomplish our goals by becoming a
member of the membership committee, by letting us know when
new people have moved to Jacksonville, by welcoming
newcomers when you see them during services or an activity,
or by extending hospitality during holidays or on Shabbat.
Reaching out to those who are new to Jacksonville or
unaffiliated with a synagogue is critical to not only the growth
of the Jacksonville Jewish Center, but to Judaism. Let’s make
adding new members to our congregation a priority in the new
century.
Special brunches encourage prospective members to join the Center.

===== PAGE 236 =====
Cantor Heller’s Message
It is at this time, Rosh Hashanah
and Yom Kippur, the Yamim Noraim,
the Days of Awe, that we stand before
God to evaluate our spiritual standings.
The Prophet Micah who said, “Do
justly, love mercy and walk humbly with
God” brings us to the realization that
God needs us as much as we need him.
Working together in the spirit of
tikkun olam, we shape the world into
a better place.
Our evaluations might allude to the
frequency of our service attendance, to
the status of our kashrut both in and out the home, how
to make the Shabbat a greater spiritual experience, and
to using the education facilities to advance our
understanding of what God has prescribed to us in his
“Mitzvah Manual.” Our Rabbis remind us that Hashem
brings His presence into our Synagogues and each home
to receive our prayers and praises thorough his mitzvot.
His mission is to reward us with chayim tovim - a good
life - central to our High Holiday prayers.
Our Jewish tradition gives us little*opportunity to
become complacent or to rest on our past achievements.
We are constantly reminded that the
time is short, and the tasks are many.
The Eitz ha Da’tat - Tree of
Knowledge of the Torah - is in full
bloom. It is our challenge to partake
of its fruit, as teachers or pupils.
So, planning for the year ahead,
I look to focus on creating greater
opportunities for the Solomon
Schechter Day School Chorus to
participate in congregational and
community events. The B’nai
Mitzvah programing remains a high
priority, as well as a constant source of joy and delight.
With a number of musical events in the planning stages,
the coming year looks extremely exciting and challenging.
It is thus that I, together with Lynette and my entire
family, anticipate an exciting New Year. Wishing you -
the members, leadership and professionals and all those
associated witn this Khilat haKodesh, Holy Congregation,
a year of peace, health and tranquility.
In honor of the dedication of this Yearbook to Ted
Gross, I would like to wish him, his wife Eunice and their
entire family good health and happiness. His indelible
contribution to this congregation and his warm personality
make me feel fortunate to know him.
Shanah Tovah u’metukah, a year of sweetness.
— Cantor Heller
Cantor Aron Heller
